Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And if the paper returns according to what it should, that is good; but if not, then take the rasps and put them on the file, and turn the paper, and make as many files as the paper can bear; and let the ends of the two angles of the incision you made be like the letters of a word that does not have "I griesche"; then carve those edges according to the quantity of your rasp, which is as much as your rasp can handle, of the material that holds the paper, then smooth out the remaining parts, and cut them with a thread of wool; then cure what we have said about the mollifying medicines and poultices, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	1. If the illness comes from burning or cutting or cauterization, then it is necessary to remove a simple cut from the papers' hair, according to what is before; then enter between the two legs of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, because it is different in form, and the skilled masters have prepared tools for every case to return the figure to its natural form; and the illness itself, according to what is necessary to cut and extract in more positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	2. If the paper is soaked, then it must be dried.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. When this cauterization comes to the hands of women in such a way that the paper is soaked with white of the oil, and cannot move or do its natural actions, then it comes to pass that you touch the point of a razor blade wet with the paper, and smooth it on top; and the tweezers, as long as you touch what is smeared in the subtle spumice, which is neither too much nor too thin, so that the patient can endure neither the spumice too much nor the oil bleeding, and your incision, which you scrape off that assembled one, lightly, so that the paper reshapes according to its natural form; and it heals all assembled, and never once in the oily cold water, and the cold sweet water, and the warm; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put on the oil fine hair in an abundance of ointment; and afterwards the next day use cold colony and other soothing things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the finger of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the finger is: it is nervous and resembles hard skin, and another that is not nervous but resembles cold waxed cheese, whereupon if one touches it with iron and heats it with pincers, it does not move; and both resemble towards the great fear, and grow puffed and puffed as much as the entire vision and light and movement of the oil cease.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision if the patient puts his head in your hand, then he operates on the fingers; and gently take the paper with your hand, then pick up the finger with small tweezers, and hold it at the end; then take a needle, and insert the horsehair, or sheephair, or beaverhair, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and the filament enters the finger, and perforate all the needle, and tie the finger with a thread and hold it at the end, and scrape all the hair from the costeit of the finger which extends the prunele and the silk to the chief, then cut off the remaining in the root of the arm at all the subtle and slight forces, and leave the natural or fearful char, so that by the incision there comes no tears; and never has the finger been at ease only, and as time goes on, just as we have said; then it is scorched all the spatumile souef of coi ci is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the charred skin and breaks it, and that the pruning tool is not perceived; and after the incision, a little oil is poured into the wound, and a piece of linen is left to argot, and it is left until the next day; then the care for what is needed until it is healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you do not push the needle, and the nails cannot enter, it is treated many times with this appearance of a nail of medicines; and I have counted many times in the division, and if you see it closed, if you oil the hand of the surgeon, and take the spatula lightly, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently remove the nail, and if you see that it does not turn and the ration is pressed, then distill from your mouth the oil made of lavender, which is bitter and reddish and has a sour taste, and it extinguishes the oil in another hour; then continue the other incision according to this same operation, until it is all out.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, like a sore, then the milk and cure the sore first until it is healthy, then continue the incision as before, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm is dark in the oil for a long time, if there is spending in the bone, and only a part is affected, and tears do not come; then it distills into the oil that is red and warm, which is made from litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that was pricked by the thorn
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men have never been pricked with a thorn, and they cut the thorn and tear off the leaves and put them on paper and twist them into a rose; and if the wound is such that the skin puts its nail in the vine, then it operates on the wounds, and ties all the red blood as possible with the skin, and supports it with force; then cut the first wound, and keep cutting until the end, and make sure you do not let the oil get into the wound; and the incision of the spatumile that we mentioned in the incision of the finger and small forces of bone if it is formed after this chapter as it is shown here; and when the incision is completed and all the blood is out, then use the oil of seil broiet or let it distill red warm oil and medicines corrosive, and put it on the oil with a pincushion with a piece of wool, if it is assured of apotheme chaut; and if it does not need anything, and the hand passes over it, and you doubt apotheme chaut, if it leaves the oil and cures apotheme chaut, then let the oil and cure apotheme chaut of things calming apotheme chaut; then return to your wound as soon as it is healed, and then make many cuts in the oil with this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you apply the care of every weak vein of nature; and of the accidental one, in fire cauterization; and do not thrust your hand into any of these cauterizations as long as you see that the other member is not ready for that cauterization.
des voines des eulz	of veins of hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins are red and covered with oil, and they touch the eye and injure the other parts.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you should look at is the oil, and if it is red and covered with oil, and there is no other disease but this oil, then the treatment should be as follows: instruct the patient to place his head in your hand, then pull out these veins all over the body according to his judgment, and make them subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be cut in degrees of one course according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then use your fingers to remove the hairs gently, and let the blood flow after another, as long as you can see the hairs coming out of the oil; and do not cut the oil with sharp points of the nail, and make this cauterization before midday in front of the sun, and be very careful in your cauterization so that you do not cut further than the hairs; and when you have finished, distill the oil into a greenish-red color to corrupt what is coming out.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot cut all of it in that hour, then make a plaster with the oil of things that soothe the pain of the hairs, and leave some jorts until the pain is soothed and the swelling is reduced, then resume according to this manner which is before as soon as it is safe; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fissure of the anus
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If the fissure of the anus is called "arissati fistule": when you cure it with cauterization and by using burning medicines according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then it should be amputated, and all the moisture that is in it must be removed as long as the wound is open.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the wound is discovered and you see the corruption and blackness, if all the instruments of this kind are made to fit; and it is called "spry chief", and should be made firm in the chief, and should not be pointed like a lime or as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	1. And place the bone of the corrupt bone on the patient's leg, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little while you feel that corruption is removed; and do this no more than once, then restore the leg with medicated ointments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	1. If the wound is seen and cleaned, and the belly is seen, and the abdominal wall is seen, and it remains for 40 days, and it does not heal or become infected, and there are no other signs that it will come, you should be sure that the patient is healthy; if not, then the only way to close the fistula is according to this form: and if you remove a second piece of bone by drilling and by medicated ointments, and if it comes out at the time according to this form, and the head of the bone is at an angle of 3 angles, and the hole should be as small as possible at the time you see it.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	1. Then place the sharp end of the lance on the patient's shoulder, and gently pull your hand away from the oil I poc, then turn the entire forehead until it pierces the bone and feels the pain as if you are holding your hand on your neck; and then restore the dry medicine leg of the patient as I have shown you, and when the patient nauseates and hardens the drugs, if the matter at the neck is more, it will be a lighter thing for the malaide.
de l’issue de l’oil	1. of the issue of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. When the wound is fully open and there is no discharge from the bladder, and there is no nausea or vomiting, it is necessary to apply the malaide to the patient; then the saline, then put on ventouses or haterels without causing pain by sugar, then put on the oil I lien made of acacaice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then drain the oil, and apply it to the wounds and drapelz; and if the drapelz are too moist, double each by four, and then put one on the other according to the quantity that the patient has used; then drain the oil in bendeils hard formed, and resume the ventouses to cause pain without causing pain; then remove the ventouses and leave the oil drawn out overnight and the next day, if it is still tight, apply the lien after the jor and nut, and if you see the wound heal, it is good; but if not, repeat the application and the drapelz and the lien and the ventouses as long as it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A sudden dislocation of the eyelid
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a sudden dislocation of the eyelid occurs, it opens wide and presents like pieces of resin; therefore, you should cover your eyes, and with your thumb, hold the eyeball at the root of the part that is most affected by the injury, then hold another thread where the double filament is located; and perceive, let the first thread follow its position; then cut the double filament and take a part of the eye from the outside, and draw it tightly, then remove the thread and put ointment on it in abundance on the wound; and leave it as long as the threads remain with the eye, and treat the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never leave the wound uncovered by the eyelid once it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hairs have grown long and even, if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, known as "alcunnati," is not other than pimples that are gathered in the oil, resembling sharp-pointed shoots; and this appearance of the disease is that you should make the patient lie on his side and the best part of his face upward, then take the chief between your hands, and pull it as far as you see the pimple coming out at the end of your eyebrow; then it will be clear, and the light will come out of it, and you will see the doctor's things as they were; and if it does not come out, you should say that it is a pimple, and if the pimple comes out from the eye it is not gathered in the oil as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient between your hands, then take a soft spatula and gently remove the corneal membrane as far as the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and the cornea; until the wound is closed. When it is opened, if it drips into the cold, hot water infused with honey, or cold or fenugreek syrup, then it should be treated with another treatment as long as it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the likeness of the waters in the division, and when it is necessary to perceive; if according to health, it works.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	The text states that it is necessary to place the patient's hand on the oil in a crooked manner, facing the light of the sun, and hold the healthy and tightly closed nail; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand with the fingers facing left, or on your right hand with the fingers facing right; then take in your right hand, with the fingers facing left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, with the fingers facing right; then place the tip of the instrument's point at the coronet through the largest part of a nail in the blenchor of the oil at the smallest part of the armier; then gently push the instrument called "almagda" into the blenchor of the oil, and feel that almagda enters the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda hole be at the edge of the measure of the espaice that is in the prunele at the end of the nail; and this is the coronet of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornered skin, then place the instrument in the place where it hurts, and then press with a small hole after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it becomes inflamed now, if it sees the surgeon in front of it and the instrument in its own hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a short time, if it becomes inflamed again, take the second vessel, insert the forceps with the instrument, and when it is firmly held and does not move, gently twist your hand a little at a time; then remove a small amount of ointment from the tube and apply it to the handle.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a layer of oil, either finely ground in rose oil and with an excess of urine, and bind it with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kin, put on clothes with much meat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the oil cannot enter through the hair because it is too hard, since there are too many men with very hard hairs, then you must use the instrument called "alberit," which looks like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then only perforate the conjunctive, and do not force it too much, but make it subtle, then insert the alderman, as we have said; and at the end of the work, the patient should be in a dark place, and the doctor should make light movements, using light meats, and not move his chief to the right or left, and follow his disposition as much as possible; then he should leave the house in this state, and rest his eyes, and then show him any things, and then put the link back as soon as possible, but it is necessary that you do this after the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you remove it because the eye swells greatly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the patient feels pain, move the oil ahead of the seventh day, and apply the ointment that soothes the pain; and when it is calmed, remove the eye and put it in your face or mouth to cover any joint, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then go into the small house and convert it into your case; and seek that no disciple should intermeddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came from the Yrach who said that in some places it was done for the good of the people, but if the fever follows, I have never seen any such thing on our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of the mustard, because those who do not know them by sight; and they are truly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the head of this very subtlety, and the tail in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the horse and the new.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are born or new horses of different sorts, and if there are any that seem to have scorpions at the mouth of the pies; and if it is such or has an enhanced horse with fox color, and if it has a horse of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those of these horses that are not enhanced, and do not have scorpions, it is necessary that you place the patient between your hands before the sun; and work on their nostrils, and gently push the snout of those horses, and pull them; so that you can hold them firmly in the subtle spatulum acute of one part, as long as you see that this horse is entirely still.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, if you examine all the strangulators subtly and lightly, if it does not cause any harm; and if it does not overwhelm you, or cause an abscess, if it is a simple one that comes out as much as possible and does not become infected and all bones are clean, then you can apply a poultice of oak bark, wheat flour, and vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you do not work, and moisture comes to the palace, which is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, which is that it has been charged in the bone, or if the strangulators do not come to cut: then it is necessary that you cut a piece of linen about a hand's breadth, and it should be between each nail; and put the malady's head on the child's chest, and let it stink as much as possible when it comes out through the nose; and often do this for the child in schools, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and make them follow each other as we do with our thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Until you see that the child has corrupted the char, then take out the boy, extract the sand, and moisten the boy in Egyptian ointment, and return the boy to the nose as before; do this 3 times or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the char; and then put a bandage of plaster on some days as it is healthy, and if he has skill in drying herbs, then use it; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the nose, or when distilled oils and medicines are needed.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	2. And it should be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a leash, and it is led thus; and if you see, if a leash is closed, and the strings are plain for purging the nose; and there should be one hand on the nose to hold it while heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the chest, the wound
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the wound in the chest becomes a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large; therefore, it is necessary to open the beginning, and all the bone, then put on the fire cautery or medicine; and if it is delayed until it is large, if it is hard, of dark color, poor sensation: if it is not touched by iron because they are enchanted apostles, because when it is touched once, no malice ever comes to the patient; and if the apostles are touched, not of dark color, and you see that you can cover it, if you see the patient and touch the wound without pain, and cure the patient of things that are sick and restrictive.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bone is cut and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when a solution for continued treatment comes from one of these cartilages, it does not benefit much, and this is true in no man's case.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to use this remedy if the wound is fresh at all its depth; and then dress the wound with a bandage, then treat it as it becomes healthy; and if the lips are already swollen on both sides, then remove all the parts that are becoming healthy as you treat them, then dress the lips with a bandage, and extract it, and sprinkle it with powder of dragon's blood, and burn it; and put a piece of a sponge soaked in ointment on it, and leave it until it dries, then treat it as it becomes healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	1. The method of sewing if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the belly sewing; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	2. of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. that the teeth of the mouth abscess are hard, resembling grains of sand, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you open the mouth, and take each tooth by its root, and pull it out with tweezers and cut it in half; then use the levity after the incision of vitriol burns, until the tooth is not sore; and then the levity of alum, and cure the tooth of dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	Of the horse's gallbladder
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often the gallbladder is incised many times on the horse; what they call "albulus"; if you can hold it with your fingers, and the gallbladder at its root, and let the wound or the sanc; then put leu vitriole broiet, or other powders restricting and desiccant; and when the char returns after the incision, and many times it happens, if the cope second time, and cauterize: if not return soon after the cautere; and these are the forms of estrumens por coper.
des sordens	of the wounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are gathered at the mouth of the teeth, the mouth is made between the thighs, sharp ones that are burdened and presumptuous; and no times are the black and citron and vers teeth, until corruption comes to the thigh, and they become toothless; if it comes that you must place the tooth between your hands, and its roots are in your holy, and reveal the teeth or the sharp ones as long as nothing is lacking; and then I make of the black and the green, and the yellow and the other stains, as they are seen; and if this is at the first reason, it is good; but if not, if it returns to the second day and the tooth, as you have everything revealed; and you should know that the teeth have different forms of grinders to make them laugh, according to what the demonstration shows, because the raser that makes the teeth has other forms than those that are shown between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you apparent.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the patient's pain that you delay until it has subsided as much as possible, because this should not be done; for it is a substance of high value, therefore there is no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained to rest, it may be necessary that you are certain about the tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient has passed, and make sure it is a true tooth, and set the tooth; and until then do not let the pain leave because the patient is still in pain, as long as the tooth is, for we have already wanted to do so with these better ones; and when you are certain about the tooth, if you need to scrape it thoroughly from all sides of the gum, then take a piece of cloth or soft threads at the first hole and pull them out as much as possible, until they are well inserted, then firmly fix the threads; and make sure the patient's mouth is open between your hands, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth firmly with the pliers, and if it does not break, then take none of these springs and pull lightly on each part, and the tooth will move as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are perceived and felt, then it may be necessary to fill them with linen, wherever the holes are; and if the extraction is done gently with needles, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to overcover the groin to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well warned that you will not break the tooth, and there will remain a part, and it remains with the patient due to the malice of the root, causing greater pain in the first place.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should not make a knife like those who ignorantly practice surgery, who by their haste and their boldness break the skin never, and they do not harm anyone that we have known; but they bring only once by the shock of this great disease through the roots that they desire, or through the cut that they make, as often as we have wanted; and when the wound is clean, wash the flesh with wine or vinegar and herbs; and if the blood and pus come out, which often happens, if you use the herb of vitriol, it is good; and if it does not work, if it cauterizes.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the teeth, or the first molars, are long and broad-shaped, and do not double in size when you pull the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large size if they do not break when pulled, and they should be well-made iron, and they should be easy to hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth becomes loose when pulled, it is necessary to insert a cotton ball soaked in warm water into the mouth for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the root is smoothed, then remove the points called "algefris," and if the head looks like a beard, then they are made like a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out through all these tines, then it comes that you remove the entire root, and insert the instrument called "athali," which is a type of saw, from either side, and its shape is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be as large as possible if it does not break the bone, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; if not, then you can use all the tools, and the forms come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two rains, its shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are in front of the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like large tines, its shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. And so it is that the bone does not break, and the saw blades are sharp; and also other bones, which are not as strong; and the skilled masters use their own instruments subtly, according to what their hands and the disease they demonstrate require, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instruments for the diversity of bones and hands, and do not break the chariot or other bones, or they perish, if they seek the bones that they need, which I have said, and guide you with gestures, according to the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-grasped to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can hold and support it; and then restore the power of the medicines suitable for this, and if there is in the bone a rupture, and it is small, then with all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not to fit the natural body, and its form is deformed, and at the same time in women with pubic hair, if it comes out after the tooth, and it is not true in the body, and it cannot be sewn or immersed: therefore remove it; and if it is with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is like this small tooth, and it is sharp at the tip, and made of iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping is little by little in the hands for the hardness of the teeth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears to be formed like this one, then the lime of a part of the lime like this is formed:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the lime of the wings we make for the owls; and in the lime the teeth little by little in the hands lightly, if it does not move as much as it can; then the surface at the end has no rasping, and the teeth are too sharp and they bend the tongue, if it is possible to harden the teeth so that it does not break the tongue, if it does not break the tongue does not corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth lodge
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth lodge in front of each other, either by blow or by biting, and the patient cannot press on them because they are too tight, and you cure them with restrictive medicines, and it does not help; if they are to be restrained with a golden thread, because the silver threads turn green and rot, but the gold does not move; and if the thread is neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take the golden thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the teeth between the bad ones, as long as you see improvement on the healthy tooth; then resume the covering where you left off, and gently and wisely move your hand until it does not move at all; and if your lips are on the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then fasten the head of the wire to some nails, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it in so that it does not break the tongue; and then let it be tightened as much as possible, and if it slips, or the wires come off, if it is tightened by another wire; if it stays and serves for all its strength, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the second healthy teeth and the second molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, if it is put back in its place, tighten it gently, as we have said; and do not let it slip once that is not firm and painful, and never make it the shape of a bone of a mare's tooth, and it is placed on where the defect is, and it is tightened as we have said, and stayed in for a long time:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	The tongue's left side is affected by a condition called "coper
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is there that the tongue is not affected by a condition called "coper," either naturally or by accident; and the ovraiges are such that one can open the mouth of the patient, and touch the maid's testicle, and relieve the pain in the tongue; then cope with the left side of the tongue that is nervous and large, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it becomes too hard or dry, and it is due to a wound, then it is a wound of the gum and the tongue is dislocated; and keep in mind that the fendure should not be too much, for the artery that is affected; and when you have done this, if the leu is red and inflamed, or cold, then put the lengue under a tent of lin; and the malaides will be touched each night, so that the patient can be relieved.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the patient's blood is lost, if they feel pain, then the limb is cauterized with hot iron; and if it does not heal, then it is treated with slow fire, which is good for this; then the cure of another cure as soon as it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the wound to be red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, and it is not touched, because it is gangrene; and if it is declining towards the bladder, and it has moisture, and the pus comes out, and it is filled with a subtle sponge, and the discharge is from one part and another; and if you do not heal in your journey, then cauterize the wound with hot iron as much as possible, and return to your journey as soon as you have gathered all the necessary things; then lift the limb from the wound and treat other wounds as soon as they are healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat's abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never does a throat abscess called "godath" come forth, and they are properly the second mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healthy, then hold them: these are small, hard, and of a fusse color, if not touched with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, if not touched with iron, then for the evacuation of blood; but let it be as long as it is bleeding, and then you will take it out; and if it is of a pus color and the root is subtle, if you have prepared the instrument to cover it, but first look at whether the throat abscess is quiet and has stopped bleeding.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Here comes the first sentence to translate:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You must press the tongue against all of this instrument, and you see the aphorism, if you take the bone and the file in the hammer, and pull it to the end that you please; and pull no other thing from the tools, then the cope to the instrument, because its form seems like some forces; and all the pieces are crossed, and one place another, and are very jagged, and is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if the cope has spikes, then its form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And if you take one part and another name, and when you have the hammer of one of the handles, if you take the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the hot water on the patient's tongue, and make it cool, and if the blood comes out, if the hot water is used, or the pus from the gums is cooked, or the fuelled mirte, and similar things, as long as the mouth is not dried; then the cure until it is healthy; and no other abscesses are born in the throat than the two gums, if the hammer is done like the two gums.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a wound that was not healing in the throat, which is to say a small fever; and she had closed almost all of the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the channel that was swollen, and could not drink or eat, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the wound was so high that it had been set with two incisions through the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then removed the bone, and pulled out a large portion of the bowel; then I took another piece from the other hole, and closed the mouth and pressed on the tongue; after removing the bone from these wounds, and taking a part, and only a little blood came out; and then she was able to swallow water and wine, and began to drink more and more, and continued to cut off the wound as long as it did not close; and the wound reopened again, and filled the socket that I had made, so that it could not swallow large things; therefore I closed and cauterized the throat: afterwards she improved; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened after me.
de l’uve	Of the urethra
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the penis is inserted into the urethra, and it is long and straight, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and bends, it is called "urethra".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	If it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cut does not benefit, and you see that the wound is calmed and subtle, and it is suitable to insert it; and the one that is bent assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or has a color of red or black, and it is the incision of the blade, then you should expel it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, as I have said, to take the patient's belly and length, that you place the helper in front of the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we made the reminder of before; then remove the eye from the socket, and draw it out, and cut off the two halves that I said in the incision of the two eyes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too much beyond the natural termination; for if you cut more, it will hurt your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two eyes, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of pain, then you must use an engine for the fire cautery of the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your hand, and then presses his tongue onto the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of fire cautery, and confines it with sharp forceps, if it is not too thick or too thin; and by using this instrument's edge, the shape is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair on his head or places the medicine in his mouth, as if it were a buttonhole, and places the instrument at all the medicine on the eyeball; and the patient is grimacing on his chest, if the saliva and spittle come from his mouth with the medicine deposited, if it does not reach the chin and neck, then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the eyeball, as much as you can see the healing and the sting of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton with the medicine, and pull the instrument through all the cotton in the noose, as much as the cotton dries on the eyeball; and do this often until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five hours or days, if you have experience in resuming the cauterization of the medicine, if it resumes, and after the cauterization of the exudate around the eyeball, wrap it with wool, and clean what is outside of the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, only burning; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and soap and origin and chamomile and balm and all the herbs together or any of them in one pot, and add water, and boil; and it will be well glued with hard earth, and the pot will have the instrument according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the ends of the sharp instrument is put in the mouth of the patient as much as the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, as long as the eye is mortified; after that, it often returns, as long as the eye dries, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of the abscess gout, because many things come; and do not do this unless the decline of abscess gout.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and make a hole in the head of the umbilical cord with a thorn, as long as the mouth of the patient does not have too much pain; for the thorn does not cause much pain to the mouth, and it is good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat or with a fishbone, or nothing at all; therefore, if you must see what it is, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see the thing; and whatever does not open and remains in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if this is done through vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and then wet it with saliva, and then stretch it; and when it comes to the mouth, if it sticks, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, then take the instrument of pliers according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer. de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat of the mouth

li chapistres des apostemes	2. The cauteries for the abscesses:
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	3. The appearances of the abscess cauterizations are, according to what is remembered in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own appearance, and due to it being moist.

car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the wounds of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the wounds on the face are different from those that come in joints, and each person will have their own judgment in the work.

And if in wounds one cannot see clearly, as long as the bow is dead according to its completion; and if for such things it is necessary to see when they are believed, and do not die until their completion, then like dislocations that are from joints.

For when wounds come from joints, and they are left as they are until they are fully healed, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.

For the wound, if it is on the principal member, and you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or if it is on the foundation, if the hole is not made until it is dead, it will cause harm to the foundation. En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those cases, according to the member, they.

And if the evacuation of blood persists, if it is governed and cured, and the powders that I mentioned in my hands in this book, and if you have any pain, and the wound is nervous, then you must apply warm compresses and oils to your hands; and if it is in this way, and the wound is dry, if you apply cold and oily compresses or oil and vinegar, as soon as possible, according to what we have said; then close the wound and the discharge and the cure, according to what is necessary, until it is healthy.
