de squinance	Of the scalp
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the cutting of the neck; but I have never seen anyone do it in our time, and this is written in their language.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with scalp dislocations, it is necessary that the cutting of the neck, which is called "epiglotis," be avoided; and this cannot be helped by it, because all wounds and the pain of the patient are in those who have had dislocations in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the eyes.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	1. It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epigastrium, that we cut it in three or four circles or five small cuts through, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut, and not in the cartilage; and they are then suitable for the section of the epigastrium without causing any harm, and the wounds are long enough to be stitched.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	2. And if the masters are powerless, then it comes to pass that the girdle of the neck extends to the entire jaw, then cut it as far as it goes to the chin; and avoid the veins of the face, if you see nothing, and then cut the fascia, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the gum which jumps through the jaw which is broken, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed since it was set, gather the two lips of the wound as much as possible, and close them all around the cartilage; then administer medicine that makes the wound healthy, as long as it is not healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that nothing should be done until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is near death, and the lack of air is severe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, pay attention to the epigastrium because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and it is kept alive; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound overextended as long as the disease's malice had not passed, and it had passed in three or four days; and then they commanded to suture the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured; and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a damsel is bleeding, and she has cut her throat, and part of her clothing is torn; and I was called to cure her, and I found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that flowed from it, and although she did not have any veins or lead the way but only the gore, it was due to the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried to the wound, and treated it as soon as she was healed; and she did not return to the damsel until she was dead of voice, and returned after her disposition; therefore I say that there is no pain in the tailoring of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large maw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernias are called "hernia of the neck," and are large hernias in a pale color like a madder, and are more common in women; and occur in two ways: natural and accidental; or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is of two kinds: one like a large belly, and the other like a hernia that comes from the artery; and if it is painful, and does not overcome the force that is small, and proves and seeks everywhere in the introducer: if you believe it as I do, and cannot find any, then it is like a large belly, and cannot be found, if it coats the body as we do, and takes all its own fat, if there is none; and it must be well closed, and the cure is like ours, as long as it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	The first sentence to translate is
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of us, which I will describe all the appearances; and it is necessary that I point out the difference between newborn and born.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that born is chills and fever, as long as the fevers have passed and the belly is filled, then the fever and chill rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division. Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu. des apostemes des asselles	Of the abscesses of the horseshoes
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The abscesses that come from the horseshoes are made of hard scrophulous or have corners, and they contain moisture.

de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans. quant li boude ist fuer	When the gout is severe

de la circoncision	Of the circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut. des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scald or blood comes into the bladder, or when there is purulent discharge and you see water and medicines being distilled, then make sure to cleanse all the instrument called "clepsieder", and it is in this form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if there are three drops of one part, and two of another, as you see; and the water is measured by the medicine which is such that it burns well the vertex without addition, if you can draw off the moisture, and then close the vessel when the work is done; and when you see your medicines running in the bladder, put the tip of the clister into the moisture, and draw it up with the clister which is inside; if you draw up the moisture with the clister, and then forcefully push down the clister, if the moisture enters the bladder now, and comes to the vertex, then the patient will feel the heat; and this is the form of the subtle clister which is used to cleanse the bladder: if it is like this.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	1. It is made of silver or archaeological, and the head is higher up; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisturizer that you see clumping on it, then place it between the two breasts to form a double-layered pouch, and heat the moisturizer over the fire; then pull the clamp at the end, then hold your hand on the bladder throughout the moisturizer, as if the patient feels that the moisturizer has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, and perforate it roundly; then pull the thick cord through these holes, then assemble the circle like you would an instrument, and put in what you see as oil, moisturizer, and wound dressing, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisturizer reaches the bladder.
de la piere	The first sentence to translate is: "Car en
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of piercing, and the extraction of assembled medicines; and we said the difference between the pierce as rains, and those signs, and in which pike we must over it for size; and in the vessel, and in the verge; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the piercing in the uterus is more common in children, and this is a sign that the child's sudden jump from the uterus resembles a sudden movement; it then opens wide, and the midwife cuts the cord, and it can be done many times, and then swells; and at the end of these jumps, the survival of the children up to four years old is light; it is grief in vaginas, for those who are between vaginas and vulvas; and it is the cure that is lighter for those who have large wounds than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	When we come to the cure, if we first clean the patient with chalk, we will treat all the feces that are inside the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never presses on the wound.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the legs, stand up, and move him downwards until the wound descends to the top of the bladder, and does not cause any pain in the head; then place him between your hands, with his hands on his thighs, if the bladder is completely deflated; then feel and touch the wound; if you feel the wound in the vicinity, then cut it now at the wound.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If she does not feel any pain when touched, if your index finger shows signs of olive oil from the left hand, or if it is dry, if the bone is in its place, and the hole is closed, and then feel with your finger at the base of the urethra, and when you see the end of the bone; then press with your finger at the base of the urethra, and pull the bone out or see how it is cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the urethra with his hand, and he commands him to extend his right hand to the top of the thighs, and with his left hand to grasp the bone at the part where it is loose; then he cuts the spatulum coping, as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And it is made between those who are between the joints and the foundation, not in the cost of the left side; and let it be on either side of the incision, and let your hands be on the foundation or the socket, and let the size be such that it is wide if it is large through the hole, and tighten it according to the size of the hole, not too large; by chance, press if it is at the foundation, that it may jump for work; and examine if it has a part pieced or angles, and margins: if they are rough to exit; and if it has a part joined, it resembles a glass, and curves, whose end is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	1. If there are angles and margins, make the size larger; and if it does not jump, then you must hold tight with your nails as they are like a nail at the head, to pull the hole so that it does not slip; or you may use a fine instrument curved at the head; and if you do not manage to insert it, then enlarge the pore if it is small, and if it is not corroded, then it can be stretched with vitrol; and if there are more than one hole, then first stretch the largest one at the top of the bladder, then pull it up, then cut it off, and the smaller ones after that.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is left large, it will become greater, and cause a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out due to the urethra being unable to close; but you must persist in your efforts, either by using tweezers or by breaking off pieces of glass, as long as you treat it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply the plaster of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put on it moistened linen in oil and vinegar, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the wound; then bandage the patient at the waist, and do not leave any of the hair loose.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you dislocate it, if the joint is well lubricated with oil and sage, then apply the ointment of finicking and basil, until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if the abscess comes in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the vein, and it is retained in the urine, which is done in a similar way without the urine: cut through the wound, and remove the pus, for if it remains, it will cause the vein to rupture and bleed; then cleanse the wound with oil, sage, and vinegar, and use all means that you know, until it is healthy; and ensure that all the remedies you apply to the thighs, and assemble the medicines under the armpit.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the prick is small, and it is guided by the finger, and it is checked often, and the urine cannot be discharged; if the cure of what I say is not followed, then you must measure it many times, as an excuse for the size of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I already have this proof in mind.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	I will prepare to follow this form and make it at a 30-degree angle on the first side.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the finger on the opposite side of the prick, so that it does not get caught in the bladder; then gently pull the thread along the finger until it reaches the prick; and turn the thread to your hand at the prick point as often as you can feel the prick from the other side; if urine comes out, then press your hand on the part of the finger that is being pulled along the finger.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the fracture is too great, and it breaks with urine, and the skin of the patient is harmed; and if you do not know how to do anything else, then cut off the end of the incision and the other side, then make a groove between the two ligaments, then extract it, and remove the ligament, and cleanse the sanguine congealed in the wound; and the cure as soon as it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the women's incision
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There comes when the incision is made in women, and if it has never happened, then it is the cure's grief, and is defended by three things: one is that by chance the woman is a virgin; and the second is that no well-behaved woman can be found who descends as low as she does, even when she is in her menstrual cycle.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	1. And the third way is if by chance one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth way is if the woman's wound is more than the man's, because it is harder to make it look more realistic, and there is greater fear. And if you must remove it, then you should choose a woman who is well-versed in this, and if you cannot find one, then use a subtle trick; and she presents a wise move in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and she is commanded to do what you command in the inquisition of the wound; and look well at whether the woman is virgin: therefore it is necessary for her to put on her dress or underwear and seek the wound; and if she is tightened, then she is commanded to put on her dress or underwear and press her left hand on the vesicle.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If the wound is large, that it moves a little by little from the entrance of the vagina up to the root of the thigh; then cover the hole with the root of the thigh against the cold ground, wherever it is most sensitive, and feel the hole in that part; and do not move the wound above or below the hole, and make it as small as possible at first, then bite on it until you feel the pain so intense that the wound can bleed, and try different ways of biting: this is to know, small and large, sharp and blunt, long and short, and which have rough edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you wish to know the appearance to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If you do not wish to see the appearance, then put vitrol in the wound and hold it for an hour until it is not bleeding; then return to your work, as long as the hole is healed, and have the sutures that I told you about in the extraction of the hole to help you in your work; and if you do not wish to see, and it is a blocked artery, then put powder on the wound and bandage and lint, and do not continue this, and leave the hole and do not touch it, by chance the patient may die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the pain from the wound is alleviated and you read it, if it returns to your care, as long as the wound is not fully healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia of the colon
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Hernia of the colon is nothing more than an assembly of moisture or white sutures, which are not part of the intestines, which contain the uterus; and they are called "syfac," and have never been properly in the uterine cloth, if one cares that it is another uterus; and this is the curtain between the white syfac that we mentioned; and they have not been seen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramification if it is faulty that comes as coins, and it is expanded that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the coins, and this moisture is of various colors: either it is declining to jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or water white, and this becomes more; and these are the signs of this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then it is the aposteme's turn, I poc long so as to resemble an oven, and it does not open the coins, for it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own cloth, then the aposteme is turned with a part of the dough, and because of this they think it is other ovens; and if the moisture is between the skin of the coins and the white sfac, then it feels well; therefore, when you see the color of the moisture, test all the intromissoire quarrel, because the form that is before is this.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the cautery, judge which one is denser.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, if the patient is healthy according to the cautery, then cut the skin according to what can be done and the fullness of the chest; then on his back, on a high thing, put some cloths; then on his side, command him to lie on his belly, and extend the thigh at one of the two ribs of the breastbone; then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the breastbone from the top of the chest until you reach the nipple, and make it all right by shaving it white and whitening it slightly so as not to hurt; then poke the white skin at the large nipple, and take out all the white skin, and then put your thumbs, and set the white skin back together; and do not touch the chest, but only the white skin, shave it subtly, and if you are not sure, shave a little more on the shoulder, so that you can shave it well without hurting the shoulder; and if the wound oozes when you perform the operation, then gather the two shoulder blades at one point of the chest; then cure the wound as you would with other wounds, as long as it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you suspect the testicle is infected with another disease, then examine the veins that are hanging, doubting the evacuation of blood; then cut the cord at all the hanging veins, and remove the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the wound is assembled in two parts, as the branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first time, then take out the sanc, and put oily lotion on the wound; and put another layer of soft linen in wine and oil, and tie it around the two strings, and double-fold the rags, and close it to all the parts that are according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two threads, and use fine wool according to this appearance and they should be gathered by stitching in the gore of the breeches, and some of them pregnant at the foundation of the back, and others at the part of the poignil; and the other two chiefs at the two angles, and all assembled the restriction in the braver's loop; and never has medicine been applied to this cautery on the shoulder of iron, and it is that you pregnate the subtle cautery cultellaire, and copes the leather of the coions, and it should be washed as we have said, if the white that contains the ague is discovered; if you take the cautery according to this form, and perceive the white at the teeth, and scorch it with this subtle cautere chaut:

And you should follow all methods that you can; keep your hands clean; take care not to touch the urethra; be sure that this operation is more salvageable; and avoid dislocation of the joints, and avoid causing pain or injury; and if nothing else makes you do otherwise, such as an abscess or dislocation of the joint, treat it according to what has been said.

Emorroydes are open wounds that do not heal properly, and if they become too large, they can lead to infection. We have said in the division of appearances and signs, and I will say those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that the morbid and the swelling, when they are present in the marriage, and it is not apparent by feeling, if not by the care of iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are in the mouth of the marriage, can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then take out the talons with thorns, and cut off the roots, then dust with medicines restricting sweat, as ashes and sand of dragon and incense, and similar things; then blow on her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the sweat comes out, when it is made in a decoction of sumac and the juice of grapevine apples, pears, and similar things, and then take flour of oats, and mix with honey and ash, and apply it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If it dislocates, it is bad.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it does not dislocate, make the patient lie on his back and apply pressure to the shoulder; then take the joint, and the moisture in the juice of plantain or elderberry with vinegar, and apply it to the shoulder.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is healed, treat the wound with ointment as long as it is healthy; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles the sharpest cheese, if it agrees with the thistle as I have said before; and then treat it as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Of the abscesses of the patient
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that come in the patient, such as chancre and puerperal abscess, herpes, gangrene, fistules, and empyemas, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, in this treatment, it is necessary to deal with the gangrene abscess that comes in the patient, which is not different from other abscesses; and if you see the wound, if you know the iron, look if the abscess is black at the beginning of its coming, and signs of fever and chill, and if it becomes red, you will see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	1. Therefore, do not rush to stitch, but make him endure as long as the pain is soothed; and then position the patient on the table, with two small pillows under his head, and support his back and assemble his limbs as they fit the leg; and let his testicles expand, and put his fingers in his groin, and hold them well on a thread; then move the tool towards the other side of the mouth of the woman, and after that comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see the tool being applied, you fix the first part to know the fit of the woman, so that what enters through the tool does not become more than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if they are larger, it is necessary to cover the fit of the woman with cloths, if the insertions do not hurt; and it is necessary that he places the instrument's handle at the end, and draws the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the wound is open and it is cleaned with warm water in the hand, if it pains at the head, apply to the wound soft cloths moistened with oil of rose or olive oil; then place soft cloths in the wound, either in ointment of rose oil or olive oil; then cover the wound with a clean soft cloth, and with it the wound and the point where the needle was pricked, whether they are raw or cooked; then after two days of dressing, as long as it is healthy; and never raise the wound and the dressing with a cinder or honey, and then with honey or the roots of lilies and aristolochia that are cooked; then continue with the dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is dressed in the marsh, then it comes that you must not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mastery is first in the dance that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman pressing against the bed, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore, hurry to give birth; then assure yourself that these children are according to the natural figure, and they are from your chief, and the second one with him; and when you see these signs, it comes to gently press his belly, so that the child is soon; for when he descends from his head, if it is with the second one, and is monied by good cleanliness, and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For there is no time when it comes to his ribs, and it comes to the chest or shoulder, and the hands, or it comes to his stomach or back, and they are turned by chance at his collarbone, and by other harmful figures; if it is a matter of skill in the dance that it is wise and subtle in these things, and he warns against error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures on how to help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally, and the mother gives birth with great effort, and her virtues are weak, then if she is put on a stool or the women hold her; and she should cook the oil or fenugreek, and then do the dance between his two little spatula-like forms:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	1. And the second part, and press on his finger as much as the moisture that is in it will allow; and then the belly of the woman as much as the children descend, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to cut into the woman's muscles with olive oil; then it should be sewn and stitched, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if now the children are born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	1. And if the hands are born earlier, then it is necessary to gently move them a little at a time; and if they do not enter, then the woman should sit on her heels, and lift the feet up; then lower the seat on the ground, and tie it to the woman, so that she does not wobble; and if the hands cannot be born, and the children are dead, then press the hands on the acetabulum which is in front of them, remove the child, and gently reset.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child with its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes with its feet, if it is possible to bind at the top; and then the nail is turned a little by little until it is even; then pull out the feet and extend them a little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump as high as possible, if ordered to, and I make it leap from thecondisti; if it jumps, let God be praised.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, if the nail is turned a little by little until it is in accordance with the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	If it does not come out as we have described, say if you take a little oil of mustard, and wax, and melted gum, and mix it with the nature of a woman's breast and make this application, then place it on the chest until it cools down to the shoulders; when it is cold, apply a poultice of marjoram, and put it on, and leave it for an hour; then place it on the seat, then stretch and close the mouth and nose, and press lightly on the stomach, as the child now leaps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child from its groin
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his hands on his knees repeatedly; then hangs his feet down, and bends his body forward; and folds his hands on his stomach, and presses his knees together, as far as they are apart; and if the child does not jump, if he holds his feet and his legs together, then he pulls his belly inwards, then pulls his legs forwards, then catches his hands; and the child is small and small; and commands the woman to pray as much as the child can.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes with a wide open hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I am required to bring the hand: if I cannot bring it, then I will lift the woman and go; if she cannot go, then I will make her sit on the bed and spread her legs; then I will stretch the muscles that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then I will make her sit on the bed and study to return the hand; and when the child is born naturally, I will make it firm, and I command that it presses as much as the child can.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the child's neck, and spread its hands, and turned its face towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	1. It is necessary that the patient's hand tints its palm, then twists it a little and lightly, and when it is equal, if it is placed in the natural musky oily nature of the other, as we have said, then it is commanded to move a little and lightly. And when this is done, if the hand is held in place at the wrist, it is commanded to press; and the hand is stretched.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	2. In the same manner for all subsequent times.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	3. When it comes to do this for all subsequent times, if the second time is not visible on your finger, and if the child can be placed in its face and neck, where the bile is released, and it is not retained, and the child dies; then cut the umbilical cord as soon as you have done so, according to what is necessary, and command the woman to press no time: therefore, it should be done lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is said that twins are born many times, but never without pain, and this is a strange thing, and not often seen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is indeed a strange thing, and they do not live long, and have no name; I know that they are multiplied and are formed by the face that decrees them, which is linked to the bow, and they never come naturally like all at once, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born gently, if the cure is as we have said, and it is the subtle dance, and made quickly and lightly what it does; and made like it should be welcomed.
de plusors enfans	Of more children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are formed in the marriage I or II or III or IIII or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all formed as a child by measurement of the glossy sail, and cover that the saucy dance with everything, because by chance similar thing comes; if you follow this when it comes.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child as I have said in the division, and if it does not come forth, and you are forced to open with your hands; if it comes that the woman is of sound constitution and has no accident or dies; if it comes that the woman is lying on her back and her shoulders are bent downwards, and her legs raised; and the midwife applies the teigne of II parts, or she is laid in bed if she is not treated for the descent of the child; then anoint the mouth of the woman with oily oils with musk and frankincense and linseed with a little water; then wipe her hands with these oils and oils; then blow lightly on the woman in the mouth, then take the leu or the teeth that are flexible for this, and take care that the teeth are not stuck in the child's head; if you find the teeth in the ears or in the mouth or in the beard or in the chin or on the cheeks or under the chin, and the child is descending from its head, then the tooth is in the woman's left hand, and she puts the comb between her two fingers of the right hand, and she blows lightly with all her hands, and she takes care that the tooth is not stuck in any of these lews that we have mentioned, as long as it returns to the empty state; and this is the form of the tooth:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find the other bone, or one that you are familiar with, if the extraction is equal; and then the joint moves equally on both sides, by moving in one direction and then the other, and should the bones fit together by holding them with both hands, as in this case:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part breaks off, if there are no joints in either of its two sides, and the bones are pulled out in that part; and if it does not break off, then place this bone or higher up, and do this until all of it has been removed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be returned by tightening, then wrap it around as you would a cloak, until it is completely; then the cope is in the joint of the plant or the knee, and it comes that you do it with the other hand, and you will have both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	1. If the child's head is large and misshapen at birth or has a swollen fontanelle, it may be necessary to extract some spinal bones between your two hands and then cut the fontanelle and remove the swelling; or you will need an instrument called "almidach" which comes with the forceps used in childbirth; and then simply pull the skull naturally; and then use pliers to extract the bones, and the child's head will be forced to straighten as much as possible until the moisture that caused it is eliminated; and if it cannot be straightened, if you must pull it through the vagina, and if it is enlarged in the abdomen or protruding from the chest, then cut as much as the moisture allows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is near its bones, if it is gently attracted, and the stitches are placed in the mouth of the mother it is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the child is in the stomach or intestines, if they cover that you draw it out at the side with your hand; and when you open the belly or intestines, as much as the moisture that is inside; and if other bones are broken, and the head is bruised, then put your hand in the mouth of the mother and draw it out; then take the gut or guts, and draw it out; and if the mouth of the mother is retreated because of the wound that came, if you cannot manage it, then manage things that are moist and light; and the management emplaces the plaster, and cools it with molasses and moistens it.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	When the child is crying, and you put it equal, if you do not harm what we have said in the alive child; and if there is no harm, then the part will be by pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	When you have done this, if the child is harmed what we have said in the apostles' creed that comes in the marriage; and if they are born, then if the sacrifice comes, if it is put in the acute limiting, and it harms other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I see a woman in whose belly some children were dead, then consulted me with another and said death to the others.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time, there came some abscesses in the body, and they swelled as soon as they were seen, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought it would be long, and I could not relieve the pain.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong pressure with a hard attraction, and after some time, more and more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised, because the belly had no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If you thought it was bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted the pain, and I looked for bones in the hands as long as the woman was not better; and the woman said she had long pains in her shoulder, and it was a little bit of wind in the belly; and I do not remember this chapter because when the master did an unusual thing, he thought I should help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the dislocation back to its place.

Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, can be made from flat or bux wood, depending on the appearance of the nails; and it has two arms, as you see, like a palm of the hand, and they are wide; and when you open the marriage bed with all the instruments, if you place the woman on the bed and the legs over the sides, then adjust the arms and the ankles together in the marriage bed, and hold the handle of the instrument between your fingers; then operate all the instruments as you did the nails accurately, according to the amount you see open the mouth of the marriage bed, until the foot feels that it is ready.

This instrument is all around and its appearances are multiplied; when you see them, the more you work, the higher the price for it.

Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	3. Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	2. If it comes to using harmless fumigations, no one of the ancients has experienced fumigation with cress and dry figs.

And it appears like a dog, and it is placed on the head subtly in nature, and the large chips under the fire; and it is the fumigations with the charcoal, and the ash as much as it is gnawed, and it returns to another one.

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula formed by moisture
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from moisture are nodulated, and grow like those that come from the end of the second part, if there is more than one; and if this nodulation is old, it moves, and becomes inflamed or subtle, and never do these fistulas persist; they are known by the fact that they are caused by egestion or ventosity when the patient ejects, and by chance some are found to be in a different position.

If the pain is at the joint of the thigh, and it goes to the leg; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of the pain enters the belly, and no medicine can stop it except by rubbing; and in these fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of proud people who enter them.

One cannot heal all wounds, but this is quick; and the help it gives, if one follows the subtle cauterization according to the size of the fistula, as said before; and the burn is placed in the fistula, until it reaches the foundation; and repeat this two or three times, while you check that these char are formed, which resemble a feather of ostrich; then the cure of soft wounds is applied, as long as it lasts, then the cure of ointment is applied and rubbed.

Exudations are of two kinds: those that are dense and like resin, and have small and large grains, and are cut at the sinus, and have one or more branches, and are deficient in the foundation and at its base; but those that are deficient in moisture have little strength, and are cut with a little bit of turquoise or a little bit of sand, and have the color of coral; and the cure for those who have made the foundation deficient is that you order the patient to spunge out in chambers as much as the foundations will allow, until the filings appear; if you hurry, and can catch them with your fingers or keep them in your nails, then cut at their roots; and if the uncinate cannot hold them by their moisture, then bend them to the drapery, or to the cloth, or to a piece of cataphract; and then cut them off, and powder some hot powders that are in the cauterant leu; or you can cauterize them as is said in the cauterant chapter, and cure them with other methods as long as they are healthy; and if the foundations cannot issue, then clysterize the malaide with clyster mordant and sharp as it is washed, so that it can issue openly; and if the malaide is not pregnant, and the filings are deficient in the foundation, then it is the light cure; and if you prick them with your nails or fingers, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said, as long as they are healthy, and do not fear the incision by iron.

Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small appearance that should be cut from the chest, and it moves with every breath; and never does the patient feel it, and it is felt to be deadly fremit, and it comes throughout the chest, and more than the hands than any other part.

And the remedy is if you take a nail from a goose's wing, or a vulture's claw, and place it on the fremit, until the purple circle surrounds the fremit entirely; then turn your hand over all the nail until you cover all around the fremit, and place it in front, and cut off the fremit at its roots.
