Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	None has ever made a silver or gold circle, or a lead or iron soldered or hammered; and none has ever made these small and large bites, according to those that are given:
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	But these are made in the treatment of children and weak and painful ones, they are small:
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the little and big fire cautery is such that it is inserted wide, or the belly is made in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a fissure or the belly is separated, as you see, and the head is perceived; and it is at one of the costae, and at the other; and it is the belly or puts medicine into a vessel of a beast or parchment, and all around the small wounds are perceived, and between each wound I must put some spice, then in each wound I must sew with a strong thread, and assemble the belly like a swan; and when the medicine is given, if the head of the instrument before a strong thread, then close it; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of urine or something similar, then gently apply the ointment; then the surgeon takes the instrument in his two hands, as he wishes, then removes the bandage, and supports the patient's legs on the table, and if the medicine comes out, as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it will be more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you have a dislocation of the abdomen due to disease, and the medicine comes out, if it recurs as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is either from the foundation or the gangrene, whether it is the clyster also subtle as in the child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster subtle when the skin is stretched.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division of wounds' cure; and you will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to their accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the place or the wound is made, and how it is made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things made by wounds are made by the point of the pierce, and size and length or lance, or dart, or spear, or similar things; or made according to the wounds of the limbs, as if a wound were made at the neck, or shoulder, or breast, or stomach, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the neck, because the remembrance will come to his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or chip, and the bone is not broken, if it is due to bleeding from the pierce or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt lightly of hemorrhaging: if the latter is as healthy as the cranial part itself when a little blood comes from the wound, and it is healthy on the opposite side; and avoids the surgeon's fullness of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not seem healthier, if the meat is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat fat; and applies to the wound, if hemorrhaging occurs, oiling with oil or ointment only, or with wine stiptice; and if he does not hemorrhage, if he applies to the wound, it is fresh at all its sinus, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if it is dry, if he applies some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	When the wound is large, like that of a spear and similar things, and the lips cannot be assembled by tenting, if they can be assembled by stitching, if I may say so, like belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, it may be held in place by a splint; then treat the wound with medicine and restore the skin with leather, and instruct the patient to eat large amounts of meat, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as chicken and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you wear or use leather for food, and it does not reach the bone, if the whole body is covered, and gushes out, then treat the wound; and if arteries have been cut in the wound, which cannot be stopped by medicine, if you want to stop the artery, and if you remove the thread, if the limb becomes loose; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put on this powder that does not cause pain to the arm when it is moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way to make the powder is: take a part of incense; dry it in three parts; burn live charcoal in three parts, and the fine powder, and apply it to the wound, and tighten it as it swells and adheres to all its surrounding flesh; then close it well, and leave it to drip if it does not bleed, because the medicine is not used until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no time is it made, but when there is no incense or sanctuary from the dragon, but only the art has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the art has moved the wound, immediately in this way; but use some digested powders, or make some poultices of flour of oats and honey, as they become soft; then apply other remedies as needed until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then use fine tweezers to remove it; and I will tell you more about this later for the major fractures.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the shoulder
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	A wound comes from the shoulder
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the shoulder, and there is no other issue than leaving the wound to heal, and not restricting anything because it will retract; and nothing should be put on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation is with the brain, which is the colder member; but let the medicine be applied, if the water is as cold as vinegar, and mixed with olive oil, and the wound washed in the same way, and other pierces according to this method, and moistened bandages.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, and it is covered with bandages, then the treatment will continue as soon as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and full of blood, and it is below the knee; and if the artery is cut, and there is bleeding from the wound, and the cauterization is successful; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the jaw, and the guide is kept, as long as the meat goes, if the tooth on the jaw is cut off, and it is replaced according to its natural shape; then the splint is applied, and a few days are left, and the treatment of wounds is continued until it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if you wish; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are well fitted, and those that you do not have, leave them as long as the wound is bleeding, and it becomes clean and healed; and if the wound is fresh, then powder is applied on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has in the wound bone and it has an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If the wound is of the arrow or spear, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at whether the wound is mortal; and if it is, and the blood is deadly, and the wound is not gushing blood, but is fresh all around the vein, then do not put anything in the first hour, but instead apply poultice, and wrap it with cloth to absorb the moisture; but if you do not have poultice, then put cotton in the wound for succus to dry out the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three or four or more hours, unless spasms or tremors of the chest are caused by the wound; and when you see the bones in proper position, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds with cleanliness and other remedies as much as possible; and if it cannot be healed, then perform surgery with sharp instruments that have been cleaned; as is necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is an incision with a knife or scalpel, and it is simple, or on the back, if the care of the one who is in front; if it is large, it is dressed; and if it is small, it is powdered; and if it is infected, and it pierces the bone, and the pieces are left to be removed if necessary; and if they are not removed, the wound is left open if it becomes suppurated, and other wounds on other parts are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre." The translation of

The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre." The translation of "dou derrompement dou ventre" is "great pain in the stomach.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no injury to the intestines, and it is not a difficult matter to set, this is one of the two ways: either by the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is twisted due to the force.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is twisted, handle it in this manner: moisten an sponge or a soft cloth only, or soak it in hot water and scrape it, and gently draw the intestine as far as it will go without twisting; and never once should you retain the force, and it will be deadly if not untwisted.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the fleur depart, if the intestine is rough or long and thin, it is because the food has not been cooked properly. For this reason, the entry is small; and if it cannot enter, then a small wound is made with the instrument on the coi, and the blood clots are cut off; and the first cure is to make the size equal to the need, not larger than necessary, and it is the strumpets for the fendre: if it cuts through the liver and does not bleed, and looks like this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if it is put back in according to its natural form in its own place, you will have done well, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then he should raise his chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound in the one side will be higher than the other; and it is necessary to manage this in large and messy wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then he should raise his chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound in the one side will be higher than the other; and it is necessary to manage this in large and messy wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to the intestine after it had been twenty-four hours, and it was then fifteen years old, and the patient was treated, and they became healthy again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the patient had a wound that would not heal, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat it with any medicine, as there were no remedies for this kind of wound in my league, and I washed the wound with vinegar twice a day, and honey as soon as it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two main ways of stitching: take the needle, and pull it through the corner of the piece; when it has perforated the right way in the right direction, if you have pulled it too tight or cut it or if you have pulled it from the other side, then perforate the other part of the corner that was not perforated yet; and the seams will be as good as those made by a tailor, and you should leave one part of the thread once, and then take it back again, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, as Galen's properly called it, is if no one does it correctly, which brings together the two parts naturally, and applies one end of the needle to the other, in this way: make a hole or needle point near by, and percure the part you wish to sew, and leave the two needles; then turn the needle, and percure the part you wish to sew, as the needles are on the same side; then percure the other part of the same part you wish to sew, with the needles on the opposite sides; and this is the best way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	When Galen hears this report, and no one else testifies to it, we must sew the belly with threads, or in each place; and we must insert one thread from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who are crooked; and when the wound is near the belly, if it feels more painful than the other bellies, then it is the belly that is more grievous.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is whether it is like the judgment of other wounds: and if you touch the fresh wound with all its pain, then if it has moved, you must reinsert the intestine and the bowel; then put some powdered charcoal on it, and if it has moved, then put any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bows; and cut the thread, and be sure to shave the skin, and the incision; then treat the wound as you would with other wounds, until it is healthy; and if you have no medicine, then put some, as much as it comes out of the bowel, cotton, and rub it in twice the morning, until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other medical knowledge in other dispositions, and if the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, then it is best to lightly anoint the affected part with oil of chaliced rose, or rose oil, and then put on linen and gauze; and if there is pain or inflammation in the bowels, and many times, if the bowels are cleaned with red wine, and at the same time the inflammation comes out to the intestine; and the perce is made, and soaked that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The small intestine, which is called "young," cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the knots that tie it, and the subtlety of all the body's parts, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the gushing comes from the wound, and it is reset as the intestine is, while it is fresh; and if it becomes dark and turns black, and you see the black leu that has been cut, because it has veins and arteries; then cut through what is between the ligaments, and move the heads of the arrows to the part opposite the wound until the extraction is aligned with the bleeding when the gushing comes from the zirbe, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of the womb
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez. de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula", and at the same time if they are thin and straight.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the belief that it must be hard and indurated, and painful, and as thin as the tail of an owl; and it never bows in a clear jump, and sometimes it is wide; never tight, and sometimes it is loose; never small, and sometimes it is large; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that all wounds that are not healed and have no charge, it is only due to one of the seven causes: it is to know, by a little pain or corset; or by malice; or because it has a hard charge, and stretches the lips, which does not leave a hard charge; or it has too many boils; or the leucorrhea is too much, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property in the region is delayed digestion, and delayed health, and runs naturally; or it has wounds or bones: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The following sentence to translate: "Or covenant that I make you know the cure of fistula which is made by hand's work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	1. Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The text describes a young woman who was approximately 30 years old and had a pain in her leg due to an injury that occurred in the chest area. The wound became infected, and she was taken to a large apothecary. However, the apothecary's treatments only made the wound worse, causing it to become infected with materials, turning into a fistula, and leading to pus discharge from both ends of the body and chest. She was treated for two years, but no one learned the art of hands during this time, except for me when I was called in to examine her leg and the medicines used to treat it, as well as the corruption caused by the pus in her chest. Her chest became red due to the injury, and she had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I sewed a tent in one of these holes, and then checked all the holes, and found that some came together at the other part of the leg.

dou feu	The first line of the text is 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The first line of the text is "Li chiés porrissent".

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	The first sentence to translate is: "Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is a dislocation that often occurs when the finger or thumb is forced out of its socket, or by chance in other places; and when it is dislocated, if it is not taken care of, it may become a postero-lateral dislocation, and it may go all the way to the root of the finger, and by chance it may go all the way; and it comes with corrosions to the bone, as soon as there is pain, and it is the head of the finger or thumb that is large, and it is the color purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés. la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the elbow

des vils	of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres. de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may be found in other places than in the legs, and that is the porridge that comes from the skin, as it does from the belly of the snake and towards, it is cut between the skin and the hair.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very large inflammation in the leg, then it changes color, and begins to bleed, as if from the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the wound is opened, then it is necessary to wrap it with a piece of cloth from one and a half inches to two and a half inches wide, and wet it, and leave it on the leg until it is no longer red, if the cloth covers the wound and the dressing; and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining part around the wound, and do not cover the root, as long as it is all gone; because if you cover it, it will return to the body, and bring in gangrene and pus or the leu, and serious illness; therefore, it is necessary that it be treated as soon as possible, and never leave any part of it behind or torn; and there is no time for this wound when it is treated with X or X pairs of gloves, or a few hands came to me, which was X pairs of long, and if you cover it, if it bloats or puffs up, and the perce jusc'a fons, then all is well; and the matter that is depended is wrapped in cold water, and the medicines are given without any food for a day or two, then the cure is like the apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And no time at this vein hands rain, and moreover when it opens in the joint of either shoulder or both shoulders, and it comes out with a fever, and it falls down; cure the patient as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that are born between leather and horsehair.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "disease of beef" because it often occurs in cattle, and is a small worm that runs between leather and horsehair, and goes up and down the entire body, and is felt well at the joints of the limbs as it eats the leather or not, and jumps; and is caused by some humors, such as worms, serpents, and limpets, or earthworms; and one doubts its malevolence, because when it goes up and down the body, it reaches the head, and enters the oil, by chance, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and drying, if it cannot be helped when it will: if it comes to pass that you read the leg and foot from a firm limb well, then cut it off and take it out, and put it in a hot charcoal fire until it is dead; and the greatest harm that it does, if it is to encounter the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or going near the oil, if it strains the hoofs around it, then cut it off, and take it out; and it is necessary to use the cautery for dissolving powders of medicinal solutions for the humors of men, and to avoid flesh of enjambed animals as food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from dislocation
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "wry" in our land, and it is a pain that affects certain members, and spreads from one member to another; and I see what I have shown you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a female patient, and I saw my arm, and saw a small flower in the vein of the arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise as if it were a wire from the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as if it were live silver when it cuts away from the shoulder; the pain left that arm and moved to the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; and she told me that it turned inside out across the entire body, as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wished for this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	All the same, I never wanted to cause pain in one part of the body to another, but I did not want it either, as I see it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had hardened her corsets, and the veins were discovered, and because she appeared to be subjected to this constraint; and I did not know that this is for those who are delicate and have moistened veins and returned vessels.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see the patient recover from this disease, and the patient feels pain, if it opens as we have said, if the limb is not stiff and does not cause constraint to the shoulder, and cauterize the shoulder; and if you do not see the joint with your eyes, if the cure of this that relieves the constraint of the joint, if like pills fetid, and pills of spunk, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the bones of the hand or they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and hooked, and sickled; and some have sharp angles, and some have broad, and some have pieces; and one that pierces any member in different ways: or in the principle member it hooks like a hook, as the liver, heart, lung, spleen, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. If you do not reset it immediately, death will follow in a short time; and if the sign does not appear, and the arrow is not removed, then the patient should pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If the arrow pierces the shoulder and enters the bone, and the patient feels dizziness, weakness, vertigo, and pain in the limbs, as well as fever, inflammation of the tongue, spasms of the language, and distortion of hearing; and unfortunately it is not the nose or ears; and by chance the nose or ears are affected; and by chance the speech and voice are affected; and a white wound appears on the shoulder, resembling pox, and then like a gout; and if the sign appears, if you hold back from treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it pierces or cuts is that it is near the medial malleolus, and it feels as if it is being cut with a hard object, without void; and by chance, the shoulder becomes as stiff as the leg, and in the dark, there is pain, and chilliness and shivering, and sinking: then the patient feels doubt that the death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowhead that does not come out is that there are no plains of ecchymosis, a sudden drop in the wound, the throat swells, and the face turns pale, and he sighs high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	1. If the arrowhead is found in the covering of the chest, if it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and suffering; and all the members of the shoulder are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	2. If the arrowhead is found in the stomach by chance, if it jumps from the wound nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	3. If the arrowhead is found in the stomach and in a sudden jump through the intestine, if there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	4. If the arrowhead is found in the bladder and the urine jumps suddenly and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: beware that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and chest and shoulder and arm and spine and back and shoulders, and the limbs seeming, are saved according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the artery is in the loins or the limb, and it is not visible, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are doing it.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I have heard of one man who had a limb cut off at the knee or thigh: I tried it, and the stump was very painful, and it was not healed for a long time.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And then there was a needle that fell into the grease of the oil of soap and paper of soap, and the needle was replaced, and it could not reach beyond the tip towards the opposite side, and it was as large as a Turkish arch, at all times keeping its light touch on the ears; the eye was healthy, and it never had any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And then there was a needle in the neck of a crusader, and it was the Arabian needle on the ears: I was the beard, and subtle as much as I could see it, and it was healthy for the crusaders.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was a wound in the man's side or belly, and I thought he would die; and then if it had not been for his position, which lasted for three years, I would not have been able to set the wound. I cut away the wound, sewed it up, and left it, and there were no complications.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If a man has a wound on his side or back, and it is infected, and he does not heal quickly; and the wound does not follow its natural course, and there is no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	If another man has a wound on his face, and it is infected, and he does not heal quickly; and he did not suffer great pain; and there were other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was a wound in the side of the king of the princes, which was deep and swollen on the left side; and it was a thorn that had been stuck in it for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound was very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it with all my subtlety, and I did not feel anything; but I felt a sharp and painful sensation in my left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was the point of the thorn I had inserted in the leg, because it did not inflame; but I saw that it was the wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I place the scalpel on the hand, and treat the right wound, and wait for the patient's pain to subside, until he feels the arrowhead in his shoulder; and he tells me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied the corrosive medicine to the wound with my hands, as it was overgrown, and inserted the arrowhead, and felt the head of the arrow that was stuck in the shoulder; then I closed the wound with this medicine, as the patient's shoulder appeared visible; and it healed well in four months, and then I removed the sutures, and the threads from both sides, and could not; therefore, I did not stop refining and inventing ways to estract, as soon as I had the sutures well made, according to how the wound will look at the end of this chapter, as I treat it and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the experts judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it therefore, and the wound was relieved, and the patient became healthy entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, if you apply your care according to what I say, because the books cannot make everything appear clean; but the masters who master this art can do well with few good things and with what is present and deficient, they will achieve nine good works and nine necessary instruments, as things are drawn down in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are stuck faster because of two ways: either by the foot or they enter, or in another way; and the one that escapes by the hand or it enters, is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and it will never escape again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if she lets it remain until the char is burned through and the end comes out; and then she gets stuck in the bone, and she cannot get out if she leaves any joints, and each joint; therefore she jumps, and if she jumps, if she perceives subtly at any point before the entire bone is burned through, until the char is burned through and the end comes out, then she will release.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the thigh, and waits for one of the abdominal muscles, or some of the accidents I have mentioned to the midwife: if she does not try to remove it, but leaves it as long as it remains equal after any joint, because if she tries to remove it, it will cause death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the dislocation is not caused by the bone alone, and does not cause any other injuries, then the patient will not have any major problems with the engine.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is not caused by the bone alone, and cannot be corrected, then the patient should seek medical attention as soon as possible, as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the dislocation is not visible in the limb, and you cannot see it, then try to locate it with all your might; and if you feel it, if it is not in any convenient position; and if you do not have any instruments to help you, and you are not feeling any pain or swelling in the limb, then look at the dislocation as much as possible until the pain is great; then treat the dislocation by cutting or breaking the ears of the limb, as much as you can; and be careful not to break the ear of the limb.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not once, if the hair is still long and even until it grows, then cut it, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the blood flow is reversed, and you do not follow what we have advised in this chapter; and you are to be incised on the nerve and vein, and make an incision as sharp as possible, either quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and close the wound according to the shape of the incision when the arrowhead came out, because it is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not, if you do not follow what we show you with the sign.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line of the text translates to: "The arrowhead that comes from another part, or it does not open anything of its own, or the skin is flattened in some place so that one can see or feel it: then pull it out, as far as the tines can take it, and then remove it: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	The second line translates to: "And if it is held in the bone, if your hand turns round as it enters the bone, then it expands the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	The third line translates to: "And if it cannot be drawn out, if you leave it alone, then continue the extraction as far as it can; and if it is the arrowhead that has been extracted, if it points towards the hair of the instrument, then pull the instrument with the point entering into it; then remove it, and if the arrowhead is in the hair of the instrument, then pull the instrument with the point entering into it to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrowhead is embedded, then you must cut through the entire arm or the poison is released, and then treat the wound as best as you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrowhead is embedded in the shoulder, abdomen, intestine, or chest, and it is protruding, then you must cut through it, and then remove it; then treat the vein and nerve, and then extract the wound, and then clean the wound as much as possible; and cure it until it is healthy.

Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	When the dislocated joint is found to be shortened and the patient's pain subsides, it is left alone for one or two days, and does not apply any splint to the arm: by chance, if a wound appears, it is cleaned and dressed as needed; and if the fissure is small, it is treated with a simple bandage, as the dislocation has subsided, because this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the joint swell, if you do not resume the treatment of the wound and put a little oil on it, because it softens the corset of the bones, and makes it dry in this joint that the oil lies; and then apply oil to the joint in each wound that you heal, to strengthen the course of the bones; and this itself makes triaicle and bowe of us, when we put the oil on the joint; if subtly it does not come out and dries out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	When large abscesses come, which often recur, if it is not healthy only once when the vein opening is small, and you haste, and put a wet sponge on the affected part and wrap it in a cloth, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if there is no black or green in the wound after any days, and you do not know why; and if you see, put nothing on aloe or remedy made in vinegar, mustard, or semblant.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there are abscesses and swelling in the health of the basilica: therefore put your hand on it, and if you hold the wound with a gentle pressure, if that is the case.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Therefore, you should not put anything on it that we have said, because by chance, without the artery; but I made it dry to endure the shoulder, then the cure of another cure, as long as it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	2. And treat each sin according to its quantity and the color of the sin.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	3. For if it is black and there is no blood, then let it be red; and if you see it large, then let it be subtle; and if it is too cold, then let it be cooled.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	4. And it is good for the one who is patient and skilled in extraction of sin, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make it healthier, often, and it should be healthier by cutting through, not by pricking; and this way of healing is saved from the dislocation of sin and the weakening of nerves, and it is worth while that the healing wound is not too long.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	For the patient who needs to be made healthy, it is necessary to give him thin bread in the juice of ripe pomegranates; if he is drunk, three or four times, or eight times. And if he has a cold complexion, pour before the thin bread in honey, or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicories, and well-scented honey.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he sweats after being made healthy, after the passage of blood, if it is necessary that he sweat char and sweet-smelling honey, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of sincope, for the evacuation of wind.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he sees his arm swelling and becoming redder each time, if it happens, when he is weakened by great pain, which he becomes more and more weak, according to the amount of his virtue which continues to increase.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If he sees his arm swelling and becoming redder after the first time of pain, and he feels strong, if he is healthy seven hours after the first pain, or after the next hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If he seems to be getting stronger from another part, if he needs to be stronger on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has blood to give to the heart that is already burned, and causes fever; if it comes in great quantity, and dries the wound as much as it can; then when you treat all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his chest when he is healthy, so that the death does not come from the wound, and this happens many times when the patient becomes careless; and it does not matter if you see the arm swelling and giving blood the second time, and the wound is closed, then you must press on it; but if it is frozen, let the arm be stretched as much as possible, because it would be bad; but leave it until the second time when the patient becomes healthy, as long as the cold does not cause the wound to stop bleeding and put back in its place the part that was cut off, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is inflamed, if it is left and not tightened, as long as the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If necessary, treat the blood twice, if the vein is in the same arm or in another arm, or in another arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The arm that holds the vein is healthy because it is composed of the shoulder.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the healthy arm is when the patient pours water on his hand with hot water, as long as the color is red; then it should be tied loosely, if the vein appears well, then the hand now goes through, not too wide or too long; and the fist should be large, and the hand should be close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be done, then the hand is put in hot water, and the blood is allowed to flow through it as much as possible; and if this is the case, do not wet the hand in hot water again, because it will make it more rough than before; and the vein from this arm is safer than all other veins, because it has not been hurt or injured.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The first sentence to translate is: "If the sainie of the salvatele of the right hand is good for all stomach ailments, and this is the way: strain the hand, and warm it with hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if you can; and if it is not, then cleanse it thoroughly, and do not apply too much heat, because the skin is bare and full of blood, and then return the hand to hot water, if it does not freeze in the wound, and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated as much blood as is customary for your skill, if you put the vein oil and seal it tightly, and then make a thread for each rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The patient with the injury in the left hand if it is of the mouse disease, and I do everything as I have said towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The health of the sore if it is of all diseases that are not good for the heart, like diseases of the lungs, and retention of flowers, and disease of the arms, and legs, and old wounds, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health if it is that the patient has fever in hot weather, and wash the vein as soon as it bleeds, and gently touch the joint of the piercing; and the vein if it is at the ankle, and through the piercing when it goes out of the rain; then the rain is good or large, or at the ankle, that you should have.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cleanse your hands with soap that is not dirty, and the wound through which you pass is as though it were cutting; then the scars will be less noticeable.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if you cannot cleanse it with soap, then put your hand in the fire and let the vein dry out well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if you cleanse your hand once, and it reappears in the second place, because the salted water is not enough; do not doubt the soap, as we have said, and then make a solution of the other hand equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salve for the sciatica wound is at the ankle of the foot, and its effectiveness is equal to the pain of the thigh, when it is full of pus.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his health if he is cold or wet, and strains his ankle IV times while twisting, as otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then the patient should be healthy in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is best if you cover it, as the wound is safe and will be mended by the hands of men.
