Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not cover it, then the patient should be healthy without any wound that has opened or been closed, and turned the little toe; and make as many stitches as you can see, and then let go of the ligament, and put on cotton and stretch it; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	Of wounds from ventouse
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Wounds from ventouse are made of horn, or iron, or ivory; and there are two ways to perform a ventosation: either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This ventosation which is made by cutting is done in two ways: either it is completely burned or burnt; and a ventosation which is made by cutting and extracting blood is made in fourteen parts of the body, with each part being one-half of the head; and the others are made on the collarbone; and the others on the costal cartilage; and the ventosation on the menton; and the ventosation on the shoulder; and the ventosation on the elbows; and the ventosation on the legs; and the ventosation on the ankles; and the ventosation does not touch any veins, only small vessels that are scattered in the chest, and for this reason it does not cause much pain, as one makes a wound; and it is only necessary that it be properly dressed, neither burned nor burnt, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as the chest is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessary for diseases, or due to habits, if the attendants take the patient's temperature at the beginning of each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and also at every ten; because there are those who, when they have to take the temperature, find it heavy; and those who suffer from fullness and redness in their face, and in their chest, and at the collar, and have dark circles under their eyes; and those who feel a chill in their mouth, and lose their tongue, and spit out blood; and if there are those who sneeze, and see through their nose, and bleed, and experience other strange things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and at the same time when it is three hours after midnight, we command our patient to fast.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The patient's head is helpful in relieving the pain, and it comes when the sick person has had enough of the remedy; and this fasting should be done under the care of the physician or surgeon, and not by those who are not experienced in such matters, for it can cause great harm; and for this reason, only those who have experience in treating headaches should be allowed to fast.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often get better soon become obligated, and for this reason, the fasting should be made longer due to the fear of non-compliance.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The first line of the translation is: "The ventilation of the chest is in the health of the head and neck, and for this reason it is essential in emergencies, and to relieve the abdomen and to replenish; and it is recommended to bind it loosely, as it can cause obstruction or stomach and intestines.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The second line of the translation is: "The ventilation of the chest is in the health of the neck and causes pain in the head, and it can cause fainting and migraines, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in the health of the abdomen; and it is necessary that you command the patient to express their hand when putting it on, that they do not cut the artery, and do not cause dislocations.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The first line of the translation is: "Wounds are caused by the wind if they reach the mouth, and by oral decay and corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and are found in the soreness of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The second line of the translation is: "Wounds on the shoulders are caused by diseases that come from chill and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The third line of the translation is: "Wounds on the elbows are as painful as three wrists because they draw blood from these large wrists; and advises the patient not to force too much, because it is not good for the skin and nerves.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	1. The forceps that is used on the crowning part if it is not firmly held can cause serious damage, and can lead to illness. It is necessary that the forceps are large and sharp, so that they can effectively handle; and by chance, if it is too subtle, it will break; and it causes great pain.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	1. The forceps for the legs are healthy when they are opened widely, as they attract blood from all parts of the body, and relieve old pain from rheumatism, gallbladder, and bladder, and open the vagina; and they are in the way of the second toes and second fingers, and make the body weak after long use, and cause palpitation in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	1. The manner to insert the cautery is, if you first empty it, and then succeed, place it quickly, and move it evenly, and continue doing this until you see the red and swollen part, and the rawness of the blood; then stop, and remove the cautery, and prepare the wound in the position of the horns, for some have such wounds, and others have large cuts, and a few have deep ones; and lightly smear it.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	2. And if it is not large, then if it is wounded twice: the first time by making the vein more subtle.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not soon found, then it will be wounded a third time; and when we wish to draw out little blood, we only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out blood, we often do so; and if it is not soon found, then it is better to cut it off quickly, and finish it when the wound is sorely felt, and for those who have thick skin and are durable, and have rough pores, you should grease the wounds of the oily and dissolving openings with oil: if it is in this way, with violet oil, or with honeyed almond oil, or with sesame seed oil; and if it is with ivory, with cresson oil, or with liss, or with chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take warm oil, or balsam, or anise oil, and apply them.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and large pores, it is not recommended to apply oil, but it is recommended to wash after the application of rose water, or cold water, or mushroom water, or onion water, or porcelain water, or any other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if the one with wet moisture, if it rises from honey, or rose water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive superfluity rise from wine viel, or from ague of the sweat, or from decoction of anet or camomile, or from other similar causes; and they do not become healthier before bathing but after bathing, but an hour or two later; and they do not sleep after the ventouse, and they must wake up when it is time to ventouse and when it is ventosing.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are healthy become anemic, and the fasting is too little and inflamed; then it comes that they crave cold things, such as apples, endives, and greens in milk, and similar things; and they consume puncheons, charcoal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Here comes the first line to translate:
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	1. The forceps that are placed to cause pain are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and bowels and intestines and bladder, because this member does not suffer from sharp pain in its joints, and it only causes pain when blood is drawn from one part to another, as we do with the breasts when it is not healthy; to relieve the viscosity that is in the member, as we do with forceps on the stomach and bowels to alleviate the member; and to relieve the pain when it has oped or pierced, if it is relieved by its own attraction due to accidental oppression, or if it is deserted by its leu; and then it is placed on the liver and spleen when it has retained viscosity, and these forceps are administered empty to suck only; and never are they administered with fire, and never are they plained with cold tea, as in certain diseases that cause pain, and in this manner we fill the forceps with hot water, or with water that has been cooked with herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cautery is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The form of the fire cautery is: It has two sides of large and half palm of font, and has a small pertus on each side, like a needle stuck in the skin, and it is of iron or steel front so that it does not pierce the patient's member; and in the middle, there is a groove of iron or steel to insert a catheter, and according to the disease and weight of those who take it, the cautery is different, for the cauteries of children are not like these, and are thin like lean.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be put on the dressing over the limb: take the wax or liniment, and put it in the cavity of the tube that is in the tube, so that it does not burn the patient; then put it over the limb, and your dressings must be as we have said, if you see that, if there is vapor coming out, and if you remove the tube; and take on the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	1. In the tube that is maintained in a sickle cell anemia patient, with no sweat or discharge, and is not maintained until it is clear of fever, and is placed over the limb only when it is clear of fever, and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without being harmed, only in parts where it is not possible to put on stockings due to their small size, such as lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts, there are no veins like those in fingers, or nails, and others like that. And when you find veins that are soft and smooth in wet hands, if you take them; put them in a warm place, as long as they are not pregnant, and have nothing in the belly; then it is healthy for the wrist and fingers, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the stockings; and when they are smooth, and become smooth, if it is the hand or foot that can be put on stockings, put them on, because this is afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the leg of ease, and then the tight one; and if you see it too late after the body's cold, then soak a cloth in cold water, and put it on, as long as the skin is wet; and if the skin is multiplied, then put on vitrol or galls, and similar things, as long as it is wet; or you can cut half of your fingers, and leave them as they are on the leg, until they stick to the leg; and if you have more to do, then take others.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the tight ones will not take hold, then wet the leg with cold water, or take a needle and thread it as much as necessary, and then put it on, and as soon as they feel warmth, if they dry out; and when you see them cry, then sprinkle on a little aloe and silk powder, or charcoal, if they are now dry.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	Many chapters are necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Seek, reader, what the chapter of this book contains, and do not expect to find anything in the ancient books or letters; and for this reason, the science is neglected in our land, because I have never found any book on the subject; and I know nothing, except through the science of the ancient books, or by my own study and treatment of the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the strains that are inflicted, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of words and chapters or the surgeon makes his understanding, and more so if those who have practiced it understand and learn this noble art, and learn to teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or twisting occurs in no part of the body, if you do not seek immediate medical attention from both sides, nothing will help, just like a weak person, child, or old man; or if you tense it is not very tight, or too loose; and reduce tightness, it means to cool the jaws, and char the skin and hair, and do not drink cold drinks, and do not eat too much fatty foods, and do not fill the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt of gangrene or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient returns to his previous state of health as soon as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient from the diet of meats that cause large excitements, or if there is viscosity, like bread cooked in hot water, and tests, and pies, and sausages, and lard, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the excitement gets worse and the fracture heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you say that the bones broken by cracks and deformities cannot be well repaired or adjusted according to their nature due to the shortening of the limbs, and not as those of small children; but do not cure, reset the large tenons that were split and joined with the member together, as much as before; and do not leave it for too long, and for this reason it is necessary to avoid large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that there are many ways to cut.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the cut of the head is different from the cut of the leg or foot, and I will tell you all the ways of cutting in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a cut that goes to the bone, and another that only scratches, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a cut with wound, and a cut is just a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each cut has its own engine and proper instrument in restoration, according to what remembrance comes to their mind; and the bone cut is by the tooth that the patient has, and is wide open by pressure, and if it is not twisted or tightened, and the pain is not great, there is no cut; but it may have twist, or slit, or small cut.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only move it with your hand, but use the medicines that will come after, and then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And assess the fracture that will occur in the bone, and the two parts are separated. Now you should put them back in place as accurately as possible, unless they are dislocated again; and if they are dislocated again, as long as the dislocation is calmed, then put it back in place as accurately as possible and gently pull it to the side that you can pull lightly and wisely, and consider that the restoration of this displacement is lighter than the restorations of other bones or if they have pieces; then gently pull it, as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	When there are broken pieces in the bone, if they are two parts, it is either hands or fingers, or a part of your finger, or a cord, or a cord and your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are straightened, you should reset them by your own hands in their places in the bone, and keep them from causing further harm or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels good to the hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully and is not strained too much, do not press as much as those who come by their own experience, and ache and contraction at the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its full extent, if the patient holds the shoulder well and does not move it in any way, neither by day nor by night, nor when turning over, but holds it firmly so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it does not feel any pain, if it is not at its full extent, and it is necessary to put the member in proper position so that it does not feel any pain; and hold it steady so that no twisting occurs while it is being restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I will tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is said that the broken limbs are various in size, width, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For the patient has many limbs, and they are as crooked as a braided rope and twisted: if it comes to enveloping them with linen and flax, and the large ones, if it comes to enveloping them with a wide and firm cord, for the large ones tighten all the limbs evenly, unless they have no knot; then it is lightly twisted three times or four times according to the member, and the hand is drawn tight around the entire cord, then it goes to the end of the fracture and tightens it less than the fracture itself can be separated a little; and it softens the cord a little at a time until the affected part of the healthy limb is well healed, then take another cord and turn the end towards the broken part, and then go back to the other side of the fracture and tighten it gently, not too much nor too little, as we said in the first place; then put between the twisted ends of linen or flax as they are even, until they are all straight, and then put your well-made knots on, if there is no gangrene or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it swells or becomes inflamed, if you apply something soothing to the inflamed part, which helps reduce the swelling and allows it to remain in its place; then gently press on your eyes, and they should be of medium size, either from a wide cain (reed) made of soft reed, or from fust (a type of fiber), or from rains (threads) of palm, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	However, it is necessary that the one who puts on the bandage has a larger and wider one than the others; and it should also be as long as the member is small or large; then gently press on your eyes in the same way as before, then tie a thread around it as you did in the first place, if you tighten it more, less; and the thread must be even, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen the works of the fools who make their laces with linen threads, it is a great error, because the lace cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it only serves to make each eye smaller than necessary.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	When the patient is anesthetized by the heads of the pins after being shaved clean, if they are not soaked with oil, or greased, if it does not cause pain.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is treated with a bandage, and the edges are torn, I will explain the treatment for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is difficult to avoid breaking all the limbs when pulling on the pins every time.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is difficult to put on pins without breaking them after every few or seven times, or according to your strength in the case of amputation; and this is how the ancient methods of repairing fractures, dislocations, and twisting were restored: and you take flour that is between the millstones and mix it with a lot of beer, and make a dough with it, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of repairing fractures in other positions, and even in women and children, because it is neither too hard nor too weak.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other ways of plastering to repair fractures and dislocations and twists: take sand and linen and oil and Arabic gum and resin, in the ratio of 1:10; mercury and aloes, in the ratio of 1:5; and make a powder, and mix with wool of urine; if the complexion of the face is hot, it is suitable for this plaster as it has a good composition, and repairs broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other ways of plastering for twists: take resin and gum, in the ratio of 1:10; mercury and aloes, in the ratio of 1:5; boleic arsenic, in the amount of X, and cook well, and mix with vinegar or urine, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of treatment for joints and bones are to massage them, to relieve pain, and to increase strength: take new oil, and warm it with butter and oil, and apply it to the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore flesh, but they are useful for reducing swelling and relieving bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of treatment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth poppy leaves, and crush them together and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of treatment for bone fractures and to help reduce swelling: take red clay and mix it with honey and apply it to the limb.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	The root of vismvil (or vismalk), chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part; and boil, and conserve with wine, and cleanse the limbs, and apply it with moist coriander or vinegar, or with vinegar.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method for cleansing more effectively than the first, when an abscess is present and the limb is to be restored.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Boil the roots of vismvil, and linseed meal, balm, honey, and salt, and each part; and boil, and conserve with salty or sweet vinegar, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that no matter how broken the bone is, it can be restored by making a mortar of wax and oil, and nothing else is needed, and he says that it should not be too soft or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen says that when restoring a broken bone, one should put on things that are dry and warm, like mirr and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to heal a wound and alleviate pain: take mugath and chevolz of omes decopez, or pennes d'oiseil, and vismalve, and seil igalment, and the broie, and make an ointment and apply it to the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the patient will feel better a little later, and take care not to cause pain or discomfort to the bones of the limb; if it does not improve by hand pressure, and pain or itching comes to the bone, if you hurry, and remove it, and now apply the plaster; then gently dampen a cloth, soak it in cold water, dip it in the spring, and rinse the limb until the itching stops and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moisten it with cold or rose oil, and put on a bandage, as long as you are sure not to have any gangrene; and allow the inflammation in the member to subside, and soothe the pain, then resume the light application, a little more plaster, and do not strain it too much; and gradually, until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that gangrene has set in and there is bruising and pain and swelling, and you have the skill to plaster and bind, if it recurs, as you did at first properly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if you do not see any sign of what we have said, if it does not come to the member for three days or four or five or seven; and never more than twenty days, according to what you see, as long as the break is healing and approaching the bone; then the restraint is more than at first, and the flesh grows larger, as we have said before; and if you see it drying up more than it should, be careful that no rats come; take the hot vinegar every time you remove it, and do this each day, and also keep a little water close by; through this treatment, you will cut off the rats at the member, and mend what the flesh does, so that the member does not remain injured: this is bitter, and if it is overdone, and I know of no other way than to suffer with pain and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of wounds, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are wounds made by the impact of a spearpoint, and the bone is completely shattered, as if it were wood; and therefore this type of wound is called "splintering.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spearhead strikes the bone through various senses of the eye, and this type of wound is called "absolute" splintering; and it is the wound of these two great or small gashes.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has an impact that is buried, or a cut or from the shattering of the edge, or from the piercing beneath the pierce, or from other such things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent wound, which is close to the skin that is loose from the bone, or it is under the bone, and this is the wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If the wound is set in the bone as well as under it, and is a small cut, and for this it is called the "capillary" wound; and if the wound is made by injury, or by piercing, or by something seeming, and lets the piece of bone enter, and is the same size as the cauterant when they were burned with the cauterant; if it enters through the pierce.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	1. And this happens underneath those who have moist bones, just like that of a child; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that are light in their bones, just like these; and I will speak of this in their language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	2. And let us know all ways of fractures by the dislocation they cause, and through inquiries made, and by the crooked one that is caused.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	3. The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone, and one rubs it with fire, if the dark fracture is not open, it is not true.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	4. In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close watch on the patient, and if you see no such accident, then it is like vomiting of cole, and admission of understanding, and extension, and pulsatility, and fever ague, and the wounds issue and redden, and other signs appear in various dispositions, unless it can be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you expect a cure to begin.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the first pain comes to you, and it is in the rib, if it comes before the fourteenth day, then you should see a bone surgeon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this way, if you haste to see the bone before the ninth day, then the cloth that covers the bone is corrupting, and the accident we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes near the cloth that covers the bone, then you must cut the broken part off: and it is that you press on the patient's shoulder, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and uncover the wound's shape which is more painful than you think, and if the blood comes to the surface, help from what comes, and if you fill the wound with softened oil-rubbed linen; and rest the wound as long as the bleeding is stopped and the wound is sure of not degenerating, then start to heal the bone, and it is done according to two methods of dressing: one method is that you cut at the narrow end, and it is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then there is another cut of a larger size than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp, and are made of iron; and you perform them lightly so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it comes that you perforate it easily, otherwise you perform cuts with tools, but do not let them extend beyond the end of the bone, and they must have a margin or a circle that does not allow the point to pass over the bone; and you must have more of them, if each time you perform the operation on the side of the bone according to its thickness, if you have tools for each test; and this is the form of the three methods of tools:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to perceive the broken bone is that you put ice on the bone, and turn it around as much as you can until you feel the bone is perceived; then put the ice on another part a little later, and then do everything else, and cut as the incisors of the bone that is between the pits, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as much as you draw the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools you have like needles, tweezers; and make sure you don't touch the skull or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and treated the bone, if it covers that the appetite of the bone to all other instruments seems like an incisor, but it should be more narrow and subtle than the other incisor; and if it doesn't cover any small bones, no scales, if the light bones are gently with the tools we have said, then cure the wound with tentatives and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of opening is if it is like the Germans do, which is safer; and the more forceful, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the open fracture is located, so that when you have removed this part, if you measure from the root of this incision, the form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the piece is turned towards the bone; then with a small saw, if you lightly tap the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is outside; if it is near the bone, if the bone is light, because it is sensitive to injury, and feels pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	When the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only covered by soft tissue, and it has small pieces, if they are covered by that roughness, and file down the scales with a subtle raser, you must have several quantities of it to meet each need according to the degree and appearance of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a coarse raser first, and then a softer one afterward, and continue to do this as much as it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair removal and subtle fracture, it is necessary to meet the need according to its location; and this is something that cannot be reversed for those who have studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the dislocation is discovered, it comes to pass that you must preheat the linen according to the size of the wound, and apply olive oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled strip of linen, and apply olive oil and olive oil, and place it on the first strip; and do this more gently than you would, so as not to burn the suture, and then administer through other linen, and do not strain it too much, only until the wound has healed; and leave it for one or two days, as long as the sutures are not inflamed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as rue roots, flour of times, powdered frankincense, and aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer further medications without sutures; and wait until the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment or bandage assembling bowels, for if bowels assemble under the skin, they cause great harm to the patient; for if something malicious is placed on the suture, it causes pain.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	When a sudden accident comes to the patient, if no one is present, it is uncertain what to do, as we have said, if there is any doubt in the matter.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no one comes to help but only medicine has been given, which has some virtue, if you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, and mix them with water, and apply it to the wound, then the cure is done in the manner of cures that are given, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is said that the two parts of the shoulder never break, or only one, because they are bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	When one of the two parts is broken, if you cut the small toe or the big toe, and close the break equally with your index finger, and then pull it gently until it returns to its natural shape; and make this lightly, and let the patient feel no pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the toe that does not touch the ground, and cannot be reached by the big toe, then you should place it equally at the base of a large finger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in the second part, then you should redo it and return to the first joint, if possible; if not, after the ninth or tenth day, when the inflammation has subsided, then cut the toe at the base using a sharp knife, if the break is in a certain part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you cut one part, the other will also be cut; and if the wounds are large, they fill the cavities with blood.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restorer says we must smooth the edges in burr, and each one dies every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that this is well, but the edges must be smoothed in the making of oven ashes and molten powder; then leave the wound, until the bone is hard and the cartilage becomes firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never cut one part without shearing the goose's wings on the wounds, and if it is smooth and droops, holds the forceps, and blows the salve among; or as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	When the hot iron comes to the skin while you are working, if it touches a piece of wool or silk that is slightly oily or in a pouch of alcohol.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the hot iron does not come to the skin, if it is covered with a plaster made of flour of sulfur and incense powder, heated with ouef ash, then it is applied with light sponge pieces, and the wound is not closed; and if the wound in the skin is small, and it is cut into thin pieces, if they are suitable for this, then the edge is smoothed, and the treatment of things that are unnatural is made, and sanded, as if plasters and ointments are suitable for this; and if there is no wound in the skin, a small scar, if it is cured with splints, and it is put on with needles as much as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not deep, but only slightly so, and it is not broken into pieces, but rather bent slightly, like a bow. If it is noticed, it can be gently treated.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, to place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, then place your index finger on the left hand, lightly treat the fracture, and fix it with the other hand, and adjust.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described in two parts, then it comes that you administer extension of two parts, as long as it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move, or fracture, then if the threads of gold or silver or silk are tightened, then they are placed on the broken lower jaw, and one double cloth is placed; and a well-made steel plate or a piece of leather is placed along and across the jaw, and it is tied to the wound that you made, and the midwife commands the patient to lie down, and light foods are given.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	When you see that the joint changes shape, if it is dislocated at the time of the injury, and then reset to its original position; and apply a plaster with flour from the miller's mill with as much urine or flour of bandage as necessary; after which you should apply the plaster to the affected part; and apply it lightly, and leave it in place until the joint does not change shape, even if the patient is unconscious; it remains stable for three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscess bursts, if we have not said this many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and multiple wounds, the end of the bone is sharp and exposed; if the fragments are easily movable at this point.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is large, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have all these pieces, and there is no lack of pain, if the wound is wide, and it is large, and put on flexible dressings at this point, to ensure health until it is cured.
de la forcele	of its strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks more often in front of the shoulder, towards the elbow, and the fracture is according to three ways: it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or it is a fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	When the fracture is felt as a wound, if you have two assistants, one to mark the affected part with the force of the fracture; and the other to extend your collar towards the part, then place the fracture equally in your two hands, so that it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you are skilled at extending, if you place the shoulder blade of the patient on the table, with a round or flat sphere made of cloth or linen, according to your need; and hold it lightly with both hands, and draw the sphere towards your hand so that you can place the fracture equally in your two hands, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	1. If you do not treat the head of the strong force, because it comes in front, then the patient's strength will increase, and they should take care of their shoulder or ear, and hold the muscles of the shoulder, until the bone of the strong force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	2. Then address the fracture to your two hands, and if you manage to reassemble the fragments, then it is best to leave them as they are; lightly separate the lighter pieces, and if the bone does not join to any of the incisions you made, but keep the strong force instrument near the one you used, to warn for the next time.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	1. It seems like a spoon, and is not too thick, and should be as wide as the limb desires, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the wrist; and it has two ends, if you see, and one is large, and the other is small, if it is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of the dislocation, if the wound is large, and the other is slight, or you doubt the dislocation, if you use the wound with cloth and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	2. And if apostemy is large, it comes, if you have a lot of cloth in oil and wool and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	1. The treatment of the bone is when it feels pain and discomfort, you apply powdered mill flour and oak ash to it, along with light sponges, and a small cone of pitch; then take a very large leaf from a palm tree, and double-fold the sponges over the cone, and apply the pitch; then take a subtle needle of three to four inches long and sharp, and wrap it around the cone so that the end of the brim is secure; and place the needle on the bracelet, and turn the brim over the neck, and tighten the bracelet around the arm, and tighten the suture on the healthy grip, and on the malicious grip; and tighten each part, and when you see that the brim holds the bracelet firmly, and you can clearly see that the needle does not move from the bone break, if it rewards each time, and when the restraint is loose; and make the malicious one sit on his back, and he puts it on the little ornament over the bracelet when he goes to sleep, to lift the aid higher; if the break in the force is caused by the bending of the shoulder, or you bend the arm at the elbow, and it does not slip out of place accidentally, within twenty days; then resume the application, if you see that it has merit, and tighten and release it as needed, until it is restored; and it is restored in eighteen to twenty-five days, and no man has any trouble with it.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the injury to the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is broken or displaced, and it does not seem to be caused by touching, then if the humerus follows the shape of the fracture, and the arm is reset in its natural form, in all possible ways that you can; then put some powdered sulfur with a lot of urine on the shoulder, and light spices, and then place a bandage large and thin, a little larger than the shoulder, and if it fits well, use linen threads to secure it; then tightly bind the arm to the shoulder, so that the bandage does not move from its place, and look at it every time it is loosened, and whenever it is relaxed, if it is bound, and place the bandage as close as possible to the chest; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days, and when these numbers are completed, if you feel better, because this is only what needs to be done lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	When a piece of bone sticks out, and there is no flesh to cover it, if it is left untreated, and the bone, and we do what we have said in the fracture of the force of easing abscess pain.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the piece
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in a vacuum, but this can happen sometimes; but it often breaks at the joint.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the bone, if it is not adjusted correctly, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of nourishment, and all, and by chance vomiting blood, and the wounds are opened in the broken bones, and it feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is if the patient has a fracture on his back, and he puts an acorn between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two costels in your hands, and subtly puts them equal to all ways you can, until the bone is as it should be; then he puts on splints and bandages under the thin layer of salt, or another light one, and wraps it in a fold, and ties it around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turns the lace back on itself, and tightens it, and rewards each hour the lace, and if it becomes loose, by corrosion or pruritus that comes to the wound, or pain or aposteme, if you hurry, and it loosens, and removes the bandage, and addresses what came from the ways of treatments; then re-tie the bandage, and tighten it as much as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breast wound
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.
