The wound in the breast does not come from anything else but from the back, and at the head of the bones, and they do not plough except because they are greasy; and it is felt well in the inquest as it should be.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restorations are such that if you put the wound evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the plaster, and draw it tightly with an arrow, if you have the skill.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the wound in the breast is inclined towards the bone, it feels very great pain and pressure, like tears; and it is pulled out, and all comes out with great amount of pus, and it is a matter of sickness, and the ancients have used great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say it is necessary to administer foods that inflame the belly, to fast the breast.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, that apostes does not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes, then the safe one.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And none of them say that you put ventsouces on the shoulder, to suck out the fat, and it seems right; however, doubt that the ventsouce does not draw out the superfluities from the shoulder due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And none of them say that you should cover the shoulder with fine oiled cloth, and then put tents between the ribs to measure the limb accurately, then treat pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone that points through the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut through the shoulder blade that is broken, and put in an instrument to hold the face; therefore, one must break the bone, and make it lightly, and then sew the edges of the wound, if they are large, and cure them with plasters, as long as they are healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. If the abscess comes, then put on soft oiled cloths on it, and on the limb; and cure while the limb is coming out of the abscess, and be gentle with it on the chest or wherever it needs to be, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time does a fracture of the shoulder bone come, and it rarely happens; and also at the spine bone.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to none, and you see if it will be safe or not, if you see the hands mollified and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you touch them with a needle, if it does not hurt.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Dangerous that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they are held and do not hurt when they are stretched, dangerous that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if we put it in care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if something similar comes to the spine of the horse's back, and you see whether it is healthy or not, if you take care of its legs, and the accidents that are in hands, and then the horse's back jumps with voluntary wind and evacuation, and when it is fed, it jumps with voluntary wind.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is fed on its back and it sees it asleep, if it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Sadly, if it cannot labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if that accident does not come, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that if you reward it when it has an abscess, if you put on the ointment of rose oil or ointment of mule's sweat, as long as it is calmed; then apply a comfortable plaster and wrap it, and tie it with a string, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where it feels pain, as long as it is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones break, if you cover the wound; and set the bone, then assemble the lower lips of the wound as much as possible in a stitch, if it is large, and the care of ointment enjambing char, as long as it is healthy; and if the lower lips of the bone are broken, which are called the "breaks of the knee", put your purse of your left hand in the other hand of your mouth, and set it even on the other side, then apply the plaster and the stitch, if you can; then draw it out, and if it has broken bones, if it is rebroken, if you can, and the bone, and cure the wound as much as possible.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	A moment comes when the hip bone is broken, and if it does, not a little harm to the head; then it becomes long, and slopes towards the jaw, and pain comes to the leg, and swelling, and the broken part is inflamed.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is when you extend your hand as far as the break; and examine which part is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set it as natural as possible.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or slopes towards the jaw, then raise the patient on his stomach as much as possible for the reduction of this fracture to be successful.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have placed it evenly, then place an iron splint or a piece of wood on top, and hold the brace tightly to prevent it from moving; and use the leather straps on both sides as long as the light is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And order the patient to sleep either on their back or on their side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if you have a wound that oozes blood, as long as it does not stop, keep it clean and apply the appropriate dressing, and then return to restoration, and tighten it as necessary, even if there are no other complications; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The first sentence to translate is "de la brisure de l’ajutoire". The translation of this phrase
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The second sentence to translate is "Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, seconde ceste forme:". The translation of this sentence is:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	The patient should hold the dislocated head in place, allowing it to rise above the shoulder, and then apply pressure with their hand on the top of the shoulder blade until the head is reduced to its proper position, creating a crack in the shoulder blade that is not painful. Then, the patient should gently hold the dislocated head in place until the dislocation is reduced completely, and the shoulder blade returns to its normal position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	If the patient is unable to hold the dislocated head in place, the surgeon should lift the patient's arm and place their hand on the patient's collarbone. The surgeon should then instruct the patient to touch the mark made by the surgeon's hand at their own fingers, and also touch other marks on different parts of the body. The patient should extend each limb to its full length.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then break the lock and extend each of the parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the lock is near the shoulder blade, then it is necessary to remove the first winding and the other towards the elbow, breaking the lock; and then when the lock is towards the elbow, it is necessary to gently tighten the threads, not with force, as long as the lock is evenly on the shoulder blade and the elbow, then tie it, as you can, and do not worry if nothing comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	1. If the patient complains of pain, and it lasts for more than seven days, and the area is oily and greasy, then apply ointment and oil rosemary until the pain subsides; then pull, and the manner of pulling if you place the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm with the helper, and place your hand on the shoulder or under the neck; and tie it, and pull with the helper and the arm, if the arm is in the elbow, nothing should prevent it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	2. If you doubt that the bone is not moving, use forceps and make a larger and stronger wound than the others, and place each forceps between two spaces, so that each forceps passes through the break three times in each part; then pull on the forceps, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more forcefully and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the thighs, and the stretching, as we have said, in the part where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the grip of the suture, if it is left to grow for nine days, as we have said; then watch each third day the link, that itch does not swell nor come to the knee, or the sutures do not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, if it is only that after three or more days he wakes up, and has his hands on his stomach; and then put the auxiliary I cussin plain of linen evenly, and watch each hour of the day or night, where the broken member does not move, or is not softened by the ligaments; if it is due to the virtue of medicine, and the meat that we have before us, in such a way that the meat is subtle; and when he wakes up to take again, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the helper and the leg should be retaken within 40 days of the entire dislocation; and therefore, one must gently and administer baths and remedies for inflammation to the joint for it to recover.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the tightening is thin and entangled, it should be slowly and gradually loosened for 1 to 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "ulna", and one is thicker, and it is the one that forms the pouch; and the other is thinner, and it is the one that is smaller, by chance, towards the small one; by chance, only the thick humerus or the thin one breaks, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the repairs are light, and the cures; and when the large ones are broken, it is the cure that is often poor, and more difficult than when they are broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bones are broken, it will be sufficient to stretch lightly and put them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, it will be necessary to stretch more forcefully; and stretch it over the thumb, and raise the pocket of the hand higher than the others, and the limbs lower, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then stretch the rest of the bones in the part opposite the hand, or at the wrist, and some other bones at the other end.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the head in place, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is in pieces, then he puts each piece in its place, and if there are no deviations that point to the cause, and you cannot restore it in its place, then follow our advice and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken to the individual surgeon; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are grafts that are difficult to remove, such as those made from rose oil and waxy charcoal, which are neither too hard nor too soft; and he removes them gradually, until the grafts are pacified.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then take the chisel, and put the powder of the fine mill with a lot of urine, then the stones, and make the wedge larger than the others; and count that there should be six stones or arms in more positions: either the wedge is in one of the bones, or in two; and draw it more under the wedge than other parts, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and be the moistened cloths that are under the wedge, not too hard or rough; and be the threads, which are drawn out, of lin, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some years.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must cool the member with warm water until the itching is calmed; and let the member rest in peace.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then the stripping resumes, and if the limb is softened and the bones are loosened, and it seems like something, then it will be loosened.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the nails come to the member, because it is too tight, then you must soften it in a short time, and let some years pass, until the nails grow, and then strip it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if these things do not come to the patient when we have said them, within twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	To examine the patient thoroughly, and if he can grasp his collar with his hands, and they are equal, and there is no movement or deviation, and he sleeps on his back; and it is hoped that this fracture is restored in XXX years or XXXV, and by chance in XX years, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	It is hoped that on the back of the hand and at both wrists there are few fractures, and only sprains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the plant of the hand is broken or crushed, if the patient manages to hold it steady, and then puts his hand on the extended leg, and extends the bones of the broken ones evenly, as far as they are well joined; then he puts plaster and splints, if necessary, not coming, then he puts a bandage according to the quantity of the leg; and it is wrapped in a writhing of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the heel of the plant, then make a ring of cloth, and instruct the patient to tie it around his broken plant; then tie a long ribbon, and it should be as large as the plant of the hand, and tie it, if it can be done.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the bone, then it comes that you place a splint on it, and another one on the foot, if the hand is over and right, then the line goes through the hand, and it is tightened between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture comes to neither of us on both sides, if it is bent, then if it holds firmly, as it should; and the tighten with the foot, and see if you can put a right small splint on the fracture to lift it, and do not move; and if the fracture is in other parts, such as the index finger or one of the others, if it holds firmly, and the line is with the sound finger that follows; or you tie them all together, as much as you can, or you put on a splint, as I said; and take care in the restoration and the disposition of the wound, and cut what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the joint is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration is done if the bones are properly aligned and the other is not.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient groans when they touch their face, and then extend each of their muscles evenly; and it is when the fracture is complete that the bone is broken.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the joint, then some of the bones are pulled in one direction and the others in another, causing the break to be uneven.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, and therefore some of the ligaments are stretched in one direction and the others in another, then stretch the extension leg as far as it can go according to its natural figure, and then place the splint, and the knee, it does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If the patient has an abscess, and it is allowed to drain, then they can return to their normal state and receive care; the wound is made in a certain way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the bandage I bend it double in II or III, and remove the excess, then bend the leg so that the heel reaches the root of the ankle, and thread one long string between the calf and the leg, removing the knee joint, and turn the leg and the calf the bend; then wrap around the leg and the calf the bend, then put on the bandage eschews, and put an eschew on the bone of the leg; then use the leather four between the leg and the calf of the dressing to make equal the estrigement, and begin to tie for form III or IV on the bandage; and as more you add to the bandage, and less it is tightened; then enter the two strings that you have tied between the leg and the calf, and in the three eschews that are there, then return to the knee of the string, as long as you see the piet; and the estrigement, if it does not move from its place, then let it be, then k'il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, if it does not, and he addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of the bone that prick, if it can be, then it can; and if not, then it comes to cut the arm, draw blood, and the cure as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never has the elbow been broken, if I put it in this position, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration made so far does not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	He advises that the elbow is restored in L years, or less than less, according to the differences of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the right knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the right knee joint there is little fracture, but it wheezes many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if not but a bruise, or a puncture, and comes to all wounds, and feels pain, and that is well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put back what has been lost, as long as it is assembled without difficulty; then put the splint, and if you have a rounded staple, put it in, and tighten it as you can, then reward all the dispositions we have said for other fractures, such as aposteme chaut and other like, if you put at each accident what is needed, as long as it is safe.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, and some are called by right "muscles," while others are called "fosciles"; and it all breaks as the arm does, and for this the restoration is done in the same way as the arm is, and the members are all made whole. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from head to toe.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then turn backward and if it causes great pain and one sees well, then turn further.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then extend the limb evenly, and tie it securely; but be aware, if the break is severe, and there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; and the alignment according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your cauterization, if you have two pieces of barbed hair that prick both sides of the leg and are long enough to reach from the knee to the ankle, then envelop them in two pieces of lint and tie them tightly, and tie them at regular intervals, and do not allow the leg to deviate to the right or left, and it should be well; and no one suffers from the long pieces of hair on the leg, and if it is of fist, and he puts it on the leg to warn against movement, and properly done, it is made in the wound or the cut; and shake each leg every day to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the hand
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is never a fracture, but the bones of the hand come to no fracture and must be careful, and only twisted in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the hand are fractured and you see these bones pushing against each other, if you can put them back in place as best as possible, just like when you were walking, then now place your hand on his, and see which bones are raised, then press them as much as they come together; then place the splint and staples, and sew up the abdomen of the hand with small turns at the wrist, then draw it towards the pinky, and if you have any other things that you can do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone is not straightened, you will find the bones uneven, broken, dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are two breaks, if they are repaired, as we have said, then put a splint on the other end according to the length of the bone; and make it larger by a little, then make a socket for the tilted joint that I mentioned, and tighten the strain; and if there are two or three, or more, breaks, if you put one on each end according to its quantity, wound around in one direction of the lin, and tighten the socket of the tilted joint away from the belly of the bone; and make sure it is held well against the belly of the bone so that it does not slip.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	The following sentence should be translated into English: "And it is necessary that you do not ignore the other things I have said for other injuries, as soon as we have said them; and treat each accident as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	The following sentence should be translated into English: "of the fracture of the bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The following sentence should be translated into English: "If the woman's bone is broken, if it is made larger, then it inclines towards the part of the bone, and is held by the buttocks; then the nature of the cloth of the maiden is filled with cotton, and it is placed as much as possible, and then the woman is bent, and the back is gently lifted a little at a time, and then the cotton is jumped, as soon as it comes into the nature, and the bone is returned with the cotton; and if she sees piss, if the cotton is soaked, and if she has passed it, then she is put back, and in seven hours or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see, take a flask of bays, and tie a string around the wound, and blow all the flask into the nature; then let the string be formed in the nature: the nature will return to the fracture; then it is filled with cotton, and left alone for some time, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the elbow of the shoulder; and these fractures are not hidden that closely to those who put on their study and use, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in various directions the right way of restoration: understand the donques.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the neck, when it is broken, take an ostrich's grip and bite the neck; then wrap the drapelz around, and leave it III jors or inquis enqui entor, and it will be cured quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the arm or shoulder, or seeming, that he be healthy now, if that the wounds we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, if the vitrolle burns, if you have nothing else, then resume restoring the fracture at the same hour, or the next day, if the patient does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the patient does not come the next day, leave the restoration until the following day, as long as the patient is calmed, and do not touch him again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause the patient to come with evil accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone is broken, it should be set in place as soon as possible, if you can manage to do so gently with your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not possible with your hands, if you have an iron instrument that is seven or eight feet long, and the length of the splint corresponds to the size of the wound; and for this reason, it is necessary to make three or four, according to the amount of the fracture; and it should be strong and large, so that it does not crack under the compression of the member in your hand, and also in front, and large at the front end, like:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "bandage", because it is necessary that the heads of the bones be placed on the head of the bone; and the bandage once, as much as it rises, and should be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the fragments cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you cover the head of the bone with the bandage, as much as the fragments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you do not bring the bone back, as we have said, if it is covered with an instrument that is suitable or sharp or flexible for your pain; then remove this which is caused in the bone by roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, seek help immediately, as it may not be in its natural state.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you hold it in its place for a while, then dip it in black oiled linen, and do it properly; and do not put anything on the wound or other places except oil, so as not to cause putrefaction and corruption; then apply ointments after resetting the bone, leave the wound open, and cover it with a cloth according to the size of the wound, and make sure the wound is not tightened with the fracture; many have had this result, and have caused the patient to die or rot once; and the strigmens become softer and more slippery than other wounds.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, but cannot put on bandages; then wrap the leg with cloth, make a hard knot, and tie it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, and if all that you have placed on it has come out, and you put on a salve to heal wounds, which is a common and similar ointment.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you unbandage the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is not swollen and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the member be straightened in a partly manner that the belly can be moved lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they continue to twist, and it cannot be held together but moves away from the belly, with small pieces of bones, because it is necessary that you close the wound with a tent, and all these broken parts cause that this pain comes.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the shoulder, or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is written in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if the bone is broken and exposed to the member, as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones of large members, if not treated, because often it dies several times but is left as long as it bleeds; by chance it may heal after 20 years or 30, then close the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of thorns that come out during the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the healing of the wound, but when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible thing to see the member; and by chance cannot make the limbs their natural shape.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the wound is fresh: if it is treated with styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, and others, if you do not use any of these things or all together, and mix them with warm wine, vinegar, or honey; and apply them to the wound in poultices, and draw it out well, and do not let it drip from your hands; and then draw it out, and start another one, as long as the nodulations are osteotomies; or you draw out a piece of bone well made; for the property of bone is that it all the joints of the members it covers; and when the nodulation is converted into cartilage, and it is bleeding from the bone, and the dressing appears to be sufficient, if you change the bandage, and make the superfluous part disappear; or you let it go to any raser, as long as it is osteotomized, and the cure as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb that is weak after a cast
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and becomes weak after the weak limbs and subtle, if there are causes: either because one was too tightly bound, and was not well-bound enough; or because it received too many nails, and could not come to the member; or due to a multitude of movements; or because there is little blood in the body, and becomes weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is if you make the patient drink herbs and tighten the body, as much as possible without multiplied in it; then administer baths, and joy and liesce; then apply poultice to the limb, if the swelling attracts to the great norrissement, and the arose often of aigue tede, until the norrissement corre to the member; and realign to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the dislocated form of the limb is deformed, it is not in its natural state: if one does not believe the fools who say that the whole bone must be broken at once, and many others have done this in our country; and these bones are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and by chance the death occurs; however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and the heat is applied, or herbs mollifying are cooked, as cold compresses, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a mollifying ointment, as well made, and take the vismalve fat, and cook with melted lard or oil of saffron, and apply; or take fat figs and fry with chicken fat, and similar medicines that dry the water.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the noose is tightened continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow movement to the limb at each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awakened and made more painful, like a wound, and it requires the doctor's care, then it may be necessary to cope with the bone at the incision, subtly and lightly; and to bandage and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs at no joint, if it comes now to return sensation to the limb.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, and by chance it is caught in the joint; because when it is not moved at the shoulder, there are many times brought to the shoulder pain and other pains: always made come fever and other ailments; then, when this happens, make the patient healthier, then let him be, as long as the abscess is healed; then warm and oiled the limb, then gently reset it, and cure each member as well as it was cured in its shoulder.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the cauteries for the dislocations of the shoulder bones.
des mandibules	for the dislocations of the mandibles.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Often the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: either they are a small piece of their bones, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang downwards, and close the mouth, and cannot hold the saliva in the mouth, and cannot close the mouth, and wrap the tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through the more common positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If it is complete and accomplished, if you reset it immediately without force; and in such a way that the patient marks the cheek of the assistant, and bites the tip of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible which opens the mouth, if it is dislocated by two parts; and the other two hands are deformed, to be equal; and orders the patient to smooth, his mandibles, and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the patient should be held steady until it is in its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is reset, it should be held together, just as the two mandibles are, if the warm and oily oils are applied and it is reset lightly; and it should not be forced to be reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are properly aligned and the patient's mouth feels relaxed, if you cover the mouth with soft cloths made of oil of rose and wax, then gently tie the legs with threads; the patient lies down on their back, and the chin is between two pillows, so that it does not move to the left or right, nor struggles to move, but gently nibbles on lean meat, as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaw; then you remove what they see lightly and do not force the mouth to open for drinking and eating, as long as the jaw is well soothed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set at once in an hour and are not converted to their proper positions, then if fevers and customary coldness come on, and by chance stomach pain and vomiting of clear bile arrive.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, you will know that it is a disaster; and many times died those who came, in nine years.
de la forcelle	from the force.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed from the cost of continuing the arm and the hip, and it is never fixed at the deflation, and it is felt as such.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that if the patient's back aches and extends his arms, and then presses his cheek to your palm, it returns; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten; and the one who is towards the shoulder cannot be set; if not, and if it is not fixed once, then reset it at the shoulder, as we have said; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten, and command the patient to rest as soon as he is healthy; and then realign the head of the shoulder, when it is released from the arm.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder dislocates: either it dislocates at the part of the acetabulum towards the side of the body; or it dislocates at the part below the hip; or it dislocates at the part of the shoulder, and this is rare; and it does not dislocate from the shoulder but from the nerves; and more often it dislocates towards the acetabulum, especially for those who have little strength, because in this jump it is very painful; for those who have enough strength, it jumps a few times and then returns a few times.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they are struck or crushed, and the muscle of their spine is torn out by an abscess, and ensure that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are sure; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And know the dislocations when they are towards the shoulder, and make a difference between the misaligned spine and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear difference; and you will find at the head of the spine a hollow, and from the shoulder to the head of the spine, so as it is with some others; and the patient cannot bring his hand to her side, nor move any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you see it clearly at the shoulder; and this way of dislocation is not easy to return, when it is new, or if the patient is a patient.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician gently takes the sick person's hand at the top, then removes your gloves from above, and gently grasps the joint at the top of the arm; and the physician gently takes the hand, extends it upwards, and places it below; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands a few minutes later, then the physician should bathe the patient's hand in warm water; and the physician should apply a soothing and softening ointment, such as decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in warm water, and it should be applied; then the physician should soak the patient's hand on his back, and place a linen bandage on the wrist correctly, not too soft or too hard, and then place the patient's foot on the bandage, and gently hold the shoulder muscle, and draw the physician's hand; others will trace the shoulder of the physician, if it does not move; this shoulder returns now, and if you see that it follows in this way: and that you make present home to the larger one than the physician; and it should be turned towards the chest, and bend the wrist below the physician's hand, and hold the hand upwards, so that the physician hangs down in the armpit; others will draw the physician's hand towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too heavy, then with them there is nothing heavy that can be done, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And this is done in another way: and it is like the long tison on the earth, of which the heads are also placed as the pin, and not too thick or too rough; then it is put into the patient's shoulder, but if it has slipped off its place, and the shoulder is very long and thin, then it is extended from another part with your hand, and the joint returns to its place quickly; and if it does not return after all these things that we have said, then this cure is made: take two tisons of one arm and four of large ones, which have their heads inserted so that they can enter into the socket from front to back, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The patient then lies on their side with the affected arm extended, and the helper lifts the arm towards the shoulder; they extend the arm at the elbow, then bend it at the wrist, and place it across the chest, leaving the chest hanging down from the other side. The joint is now realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	If the joint is realigned in this manner, if it comes to pass that you place a ball of thread equal to the size of the arm on one side, then place a powdered spice spray on the other side, with incense and vinegar, all along the shoulder blade and down the back, then tighten the thread on one side, turn the limb over the spray, and wrap the hand around the arm, and let the hand remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he takes a small amount, as the limb is comfortable, for it heals faster; and then he should take more after the fourth or seventh day, and move it; and if it is tight and not softened, it is healthy.
