And if the dislocation is in the back, and it cannot be extended the painful limb strongly, do not lift it from the ground, but it should be as it was when it was dislocated in the back; put it on your face, and extend it as we have said before, and it must press on the joint at the table; and it will be enough when the painful limb extends its legs and they are equal; then bend the knees, and place the plaster, and hold it with a bendable, if the limb does not move; and rest for three or four hours, then remove the plaster, and see if the legs are equal, if the stretch, as we have said before, and leave them for three or four hours, then remove the plaster, and let the element go as long as the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder's dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it should not be pulled to the front, and only from the side and downwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and it does not bend at the knee, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is when you make the patient straight, and extend the leg if possible, and put your back against their face, and put their foot on their feet; then take the shoulder with your hands, and stretch between your two fingers, and bend the two lower joints of the shoulder; and other means extend the foot, as long as the shoulder returns to its place, and the signs are that the leg is bent at the knee lightly; and apply the plaster, and make the leg airtight at the knee, and gather the fingers together firmly for three or four times, then remove it; and do not move the patient's shoulder for any reason until the member is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not present, then extend the treatment firmly, as we have said in the treatment of the wound, as long as it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is never twisted, and never completely dislocated, and it is difficult to mend.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if the sign is that the ankle is dislocated, and try before to the part where it is dislocated: the reductions are lighter, and it should be stretched gently with the hands when it is only unstable.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And if the ankle is completely dislocated, and try before to the part where it is dislocated: the reductions are lighter, and it should be stretched gently with the hands when it is only unstable. Then sit the patient on the bed, and pull the leg towards you with one hand, and then with the other, raise the foot, and hold it firmly with your thumb; then do this twice, then raise it high and hold it there firmly; if it returns, that's good; if not, if it doesn't return, then set the ankle back in its place on the ground, and keep the knee firmly on the ground between the knees, and let the ankle lie flat so that it does not twist the ankle; then mark the position of the knee with your other hand, and extend the leg equally to the other side of the ankle; then stretch each of the hands equally, and the patient should be held between the knees to hold the ankle in place; then put the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg on the other side, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	1. And when it reaches the point, if you apply plaster and let it dry, and form the bandage, and tie it to the leg, and wrap the nerves that are under the ankle bone, so that the laces are not too tight; then leave it on for II or III days, and if the laces are loose, then reapply; then remove it at the end of the fourth or fifth day, and apply a new one every four days; and if it does not reach the end of this process, it is a shame that it has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if an abscess forms, it comes, and if you can calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, as soon as it is healthy.
des dois	The first line of the text is 
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they can be extended well with effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no painful position of the shoulder, and it can be reset either above or below the joint, then place your hand on the bone that has opened, press on the bone with your hand as it returns to its place; and when it is equalized, and there are no openings, if you put a table on the outside of the shoulder at the head of the arm, then form the hand, and let it go, and rest; and make him rest until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocation, and they are seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your care, if you are not rough and unmerciful and slow, and if you are pitiful and merciful and tardy, do not be hard-hearted. And begin with soothing measures for the abscess, and let the patient hold the member in your hand, if you see hope for health; and when you see hope, immediately set the member at the joint, even if the abscess is coming out and vieging; and when the members are at the joint, if there is need for soothing measures for the wound, and to heal the dislocation, and if there is a fracture, and the bones are broken, and you do as we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into the way of despair, according to what we have said, because this is good according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your heart and soul.
